واعلم أن الوجوب يقال على الواجب باعتبار ما له من الخواص، وهي ثلاث : فالأولى استغناؤه ( في وجوده ( عن الغير)، وقد عبر عنها بعدم احتياجه أو بعدم توقفه فيه على غيره ( الثانية : كون ذاته مقتضية لوجوده ) اقتضاء تاماً . ( الثالثة : الشيء الذي يمتاز به الذات عن الغير)، وإطلاق الوجوب على المعنيين الأولين ظاهر مشهور، وأما إطلاقه على الثالث فإما بتأويل الواجب، أو إرادة مبدأ الوجوب .
قوله : ( واعلم أن الوجوب إلخ) يعني أن الوجوب بالمعنى الضروري هو كيفية نسبة الوجود، فهو صفة للنسبة ولا يوصف به ذاته تعالى وإلا لكان وصفاً بحال متعلقة، بل إنما يوصف به باعتبار استعماله في أحد المعاني الثلاثة التي تختص بذاته تعالى، لكون هذه المفهومات لازمة لذلك المعنى الذي هو صفة النسبة إما بطريق المجاز، أو بطريق الأشتراك .
قوله : ( الشيء الذي إلخ) أي هذا المفهوم ليصح كونه خاصة له تعالى، ولذا زاد لفظ الشيء، والمراد بالغير كل ما يغايره حتى صفاته، وليس ذلك الشيء إلا ذاته الشخصية فلا يصدق هذا المعنى على غيره أصلا. فما قيل إنه يصدق على صفاته تعالى فلا يكون بهذا المعنى عين وهم، وكذا الحال في الإمكان .
قوله : (ظاهر مشهور ولا شبهة في وصف ذاته تعالى بالوجوب بهذين المعنيين اشتقاقاً لكونهما قائمين بذاته تعالى .
قوله : ( واعلم أن الوجوب يقال على الواجب) أي يطلق عليه بالاشتقاق فيقال: الله تعالى واجب أو ذو وجوب أي ذو استغناء في وجوده عن الغير، وهكذا.
قوله : ( الثالثة الشيء الذي إلخ قيل : هذا أعم من الأولين لصدقه عليهما وعلى غيرهما من نفس الذات ومن سائر الصفات المختصة به ،تعالى إلا أن يراد بالشيء الموجود، وامتياز الذات بالذات لا يقدح في القول بامتيازه بالصفة أيضاً، فكون الخاصة الثالثة عين الذات إنما
( وهي ) أي هذه الخواص (أمورٌ متلازمة لكنها متغايرة في المفهوم) أما تغايرها فلان الخاصة الثالثة عين الذات فإنه تعالى بذاته متميز عن جميع ما عداه، والثانية نسبة الذات والوجود والأولى نسبة سلبية مترتبة على النسبة الثبوتية، وأما بین تلازمها فلأنه كان ذاته كافيا في اقتضاء وجوده لم يحتج في وجوده إلى غيره، وبالعكس. ومتى وجد أحد هذين الأمرين وجد ما به يتميز الذات عن الغير وبالعكس. ( فافهم هذا الذي ذكرناه من معاني الوجوب، وليكن هذا على ذكر منك ) فإنه ينفعك ( فيما يرد عليك من أحكامه ) أي أحكام الوجوب من كونه وجودياً أو عدمياً وكونه عين الذات أو زائدا عليها فالمعنى الأول عدمي والأخيران وجوديان بمعنى أنه لا سلب في مفهومهما والثالث عين الذات بخلاف الأولين (وكذا الإمكان) يقال
قوله: (فإما بتأويل الواجب إلخ) إذ ليس الوجوب بذلك المعنى قائماً بذاته تعالى حتى يوصف بما يشتق منه بل هو محمول عليه مواطأة فلا بد من تأويل الوجود بالواجب على التسامح المشهور من ذكر المشتق منه وإرادة المشتق أو يراد بالوجوب مبدؤه على طريق ذكر المسبب وإرادة السبب وعلى التقديرين يكون الوجوب عبارة كون الشيء بحيث يمتاز عن غيره، فتدبر فإنه مما زل فيه إقدام .
قوله : ( لكنها متغايرة في المفهوم والتلازم لا يستلزم التغاير في المفهوم حتى لا الاستدراك على ما وهم لتحقق التلازم مع التغاير بالاعتبار كما في الحد والمحدود. قوله : ( فلأنه إلخ ) فالتلازم بينهما باعتبار التحقق .
قوله: (فيما يرد عليك سواء كان مذكوراً في هذا الكتاب أولا، فلا يرد أن الوجودي والعدمي بالمعنى الذي ذكره الشارح قدس سره ليس مذكوراً في الكتاب، إنما المذكور بمعنى الموجود والمعدوم وهو ليس متفرعا على اختلاف المعاني .
قوله : ( والثالث عين الذات أي صدقاً بخلاف الأولين فإنهما يغايرانه صدقاً وإن كانا عين الذات خارجاً بمعنى أنهما ليسا زائدين عليه في الخارج. قوله : ( وكذا الإمكان إلخ وكذا الامتناع إلا أنه لا كمال في معرفة أحواله، فلذا ترك بيانه .
يسلم بمعنى الصدق عليه، ولك أن تقول : إطلاق الوجوب على المعنى الثالث اصطلاح الفلاسفة النافين للصفات، وأما المعنيان الأولان للوجوب فخروجهما إما تحمل الشيء على الموجود مجازاً أو بحصر سببية لامتيازية في الشيء المستفاد من القديم به مريداً بالامتياز الامتياز الذاتي فتأمل.
قوله : (لكنها متغايرة فإن قلت : التلازم يقتضي التغاير بدون العكس فلا حاجة لقوله أمور متلازمة لكنها متغايرة قلت : كأنه لاحظ أن التلازم يكفيه التغاير الاعتباري كما بين الحد والمحدود ومراده هاهنا التغاير الذاتي، فلذا صرح بالتغاير بعد الحكم باللازم، نعم لو قال متغايرة متلازمة كما ذكره الشارح في معاني الإمكان لكان أظهر.
قوله : ( وكذا الإمكان قيل وكذا الامتناع يدل على الممتنع باعتبار ما له من الخواص
And know that wujub is said of the Necessary Being in consideration of its properties, which are three: The first is its independence (in its existence) from other than it, and it has been expressed by its not needing or its not depending in its existence on other than it. The second: that its essence is what necessitates its existence, a complete necessitation. The third: the thing by which the essence is distinguished from other than it. And applying wujub to the first two meanings is apparent and well-known. As for applying it to the third, it is either by interpreting 'the Necessary Being' or intending the source of wujub.
He said: (And know that wujub etc.) Meaning that wujub in the essential sense is the modality of the relation of existence, so it is an attribute of the relation, and His essence (exalted) is not described by it, otherwise it would be a description by a state of something related. Rather, He is described by it only in consideration of its usage in one of the three meanings that are specific to His essence, because these concepts are necessary to that meaning which is the attribute of the relation, either metaphorically or by homonymy.
He said: (The thing which etc.) That is, this concept in order to be correct as a property specific to Him (exalted), and therefore he added the word 'thing'. And by 'other than it' is meant everything that is other than Him, even His attributes. And that thing is nothing but His personal essence, so this meaning does not apply to other than Him at all. So what is said that it applies to His attributes (exalted) is pure illusion, and likewise in the case of imkan.
He said: (Apparent and well-known, and no doubt in describing His essence (exalted) by wujub in these two meanings by derivation because they are subsisting in His essence.
He said: (And know that wujub is said of the wajib) that is, it is applied to it by derivation, so it is said: God (exalted) is wajib or possesses wujub, i.e., possesses independence in His existence from other than Him, and so on.
He said: (The third: the thing which etc.) It was said: This is more general than the first two because it applies to them and to other than them from the essence itself and from all the other attributes specific to Him (exalted), unless what is meant by 'thing' is existent. And the distinction of the essence by the essence does not impair the statement of its distinction by the attribute also. So that the third property being identical to the essence is only...
(And they) i.e., these properties (are mutually implying things but different in concept). As for their difference, it is because the third property is identical to the essence, for He (exalted) is distinguished by His essence from all that is other than Him; the second is the relation of the essence and existence; and the first is a negative relation consequent upon the positive relation. As for their mutual implication, it is because if His essence is sufficient in necessitating His existence, it does not need in its existence other than it, and vice versa. And whenever one of these two matters is found, what distinguishes the essence from other than it is found, and vice versa. (So understand what we have mentioned of the meanings of wujub, and let this be on your mind) for it will benefit you (in what comes to you of its rulings), i.e., the rulings of wujub, such as whether it is existential or non-existential, and whether it is identical to the essence or additional. So the first meaning is non-existential, and the last two are existential, meaning that there is no negation in their concept. And the third is identical to the essence, unlike the first two. (And likewise imkan) is said.
He said: (For either by interpreting 'the wajib' etc.) For wujub in that sense is not subsisting in His essence (exalted) such that He is described by what is derived from it; rather, it is predicated upon it by conformity. So it is necessary to interpret 'existence' as 'the wajib' according to the well-known license of mentioning the noun from which something is derived and intending the derived term, or what is meant by wujub is its source, by way of mentioning the effect and intending the cause. On both estimations, wujub becomes the expression of the thing being such that it is distinguished from other than it. So contemplate, for it is something in which feet have slipped.
He said: (But they are different in concept, and mutual implication does not entail difference in concept, so that there is no) correction of what was imagined, because mutual implication can coexist with difference by consideration, as in the case of definition and definiendum.
He said: (For because etc.) So the mutual implication between them is in terms of realization.
He said: (In what comes to you, whether it is mentioned in this book or not, so it is not objected that the existential and non-existential in the sense mentioned by the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) are not mentioned in the book. What is mentioned is in the sense of existent and non-existent, which is not a branch of the difference of meanings.
He said: (And the third is identical to the essence) meaning in truth [literally: in truth], unlike the first two, for they differ from it in truth, even though they are identical to the essence externally, meaning that they are not additional to it in external reality.
He said: (And likewise imkan etc.) And likewise imtina', except that there is no completeness in knowing its states, so its explanation was left.
It is accepted in the sense of being true of it. But you may say: The application of wujub to the third meaning is the terminology of the philosophers who negate the attributes. As for the first two meanings of wujub, their being applied is either by carrying the thing upon the existent metaphorically, or by restricting causality for distinctiveness in the thing derived from the eternal, intending by distinctiveness the essential distinctiveness, so contemplate.
He said: (But they are different. If you say: Mutual implication necessitates difference without the converse, so there is no need for his saying 'things mutually implying but different'. I say: It is as if he noticed that mutual implication suffices for conceptual difference as between definition and definiendum, and his intention here is essential difference, so he explicitly mentioned difference after the judgment of implication. Yes, if he had said 'different, mutually implying' as the commentator mentioned in the meanings of imkan, it would have been more apparent.
He said: (And likewise imkan) it was said: And likewise imtina' indicates the impossible in consideration of its properties.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the three properties (khawass) of wujub in relation to the Necessary Being (al-wajib). It begins with the matn statement that wujub is said of the wajib in terms of its three properties: (1) independence from others in existence, (2) the essence itself necessitates existence completely, and (3) the thing by which the essence is distinguished from others. The first two are well-known, while the third requires interpretation. The commentary then explains that wujub in the essential sense is an attribute of the relation of existence, not directly of God's essence; rather, God is described by wujub through one of these three meanings. The first two meanings are applied to God by derivation (ishtiqaq) – e.g., 'God is wajib' meaning He is independent. The third meaning is more subtle: it is either a metaphorical application of 'wajib' to mean the thing that possesses the property of distinction, or it refers to the source of wujub. The passage then discusses the mutual implication (talazum) among the three properties: they are mutually implying but distinct in concept (mutaghayira fi al-mafhum). The third property is the essence itself, the second is the relation of essence to existence, and the first is a negative relation dependent on the positive one. The mutual implication is explained: if the essence is sufficient for existence, then it does not need others, and vice versa. Also, if either of the first two properties holds, the distinguishing property follows. The passage concludes with advice to remember this for rulings on wujub – e.g., whether the first property is non-existential ('adami) while the others are existential (wujudi), and whether the third is identical to the essence (ayn al-dhat) while the first two are not, though they are not additional to the essence externally. Finally, the same analysis applies to imkan (possibility) and imtina' (impossibility), but the latter is less important.

Key Terms
الخواص (khawass)
الاستغناء (al-istighna')
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida')
الامتياز (al-imtiyaz)
الوجوب (wujub)
الواجب (al-wajib)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the third property is entirely distinct from the first two and has a straightforward application.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that applying wujub to the third property is either by interpreting 'wajib' or by intending the source of wujub, showing it is less direct.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two properties of wujub are 'apparent and well-known'?
A) The first and second
B) The second and third
C) The first and third
D) All three

Key Takeaway
The Necessary Being is described by three properties under wujub: independence, self-sufficiency, and distinction, with the first two being straightforwardly applicable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you truly rely on God's independence (that He needs nothing) or do you secretly depend on people, wealth, or status for your sense of security? What would change if you fully lived in the reality that God is completely independent and you are utterly dependent on Him?
?
The second property teaches that God's essence necessitates His existence — He is self-sufficient by His very nature. Are there areas in your life where you try to make yourself 'self-sufficient' apart from God? How can you actively depend on Him in those areas today?
?
The third property is about distinction: God is distinct from all creation. In what ways do you seek distinction or uniqueness apart from God? How can you redirect your desire for distinction to glorify Him as the only One truly distinct, and find your identity in being His servant?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

Mutual Implication and Conceptual Difference of the Properties
Explanation of the relationships among the three properties and their implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the three properties of wujub are mutually implying but conceptually distinct, and how this relates to the rulings of wujub.

Core Idea
The three properties are necessarily connected but differ in meaning and ontological status.

After defining the three properties, the passage delves into their interrelationship. They are mutually implying (mutalazima) but different in concept (mutaghayira fi al-mafhum). The commentary explains the reason for their difference and implication, and then applies this to rulings like whether wujub is existential or non-existential.

Guided Path
1
Read the section on mutual implication
Read the passage that states the properties are mutually implying but different in concept. Notice the explanation of why they differ.
The third property is the essence itself, the second is a relation, the first is a negative relation.
2
Understand the mutual implication
The passage explains that if the essence is sufficient for existence, it does not need others; and if it is independent, it must be self-sufficient. Both imply distinction.
This is a logical entailment.
3
Learn the rulings of wujub
The passage then applies this to rulings: the first property is non-existential (a negation), the last two are existential (positive concepts). The third is identical to the essence, while the first two are not, though they are not additional externally.
This distinguishes the ontological status of each property.

قوله : ( واعلم أن الوجوب يقال على الواجب) أي يطلق عليه بالاشتقاق فيقال: الله تعالى واجب أو ذو وجوب أي ذو استغناء في وجوده عن الغير، وهكذا.
قوله : ( الثالثة الشيء الذي إلخ قيل : هذا أعم من الأولين لصدقه عليهما وعلى غيرهما من نفس الذات ومن سائر الصفات المختصة به ،تعالى إلا أن يراد بالشيء الموجود، وامتياز الذات بالذات لا يقدح في القول بامتيازه بالصفة أيضاً، فكون الخاصة الثالثة عين الذات إنما
( وهي ) أي هذه الخواص (أمورٌ متلازمة لكنها متغايرة في المفهوم) أما تغايرها فلان الخاصة الثالثة عين الذات فإنه تعالى بذاته متميز عن جميع ما عداه، والثانية نسبة الذات والوجود والأولى نسبة سلبية مترتبة على النسبة الثبوتية، وأما بین تلازمها فلأنه كان ذاته كافيا في اقتضاء وجوده لم يحتج في وجوده إلى غيره، وبالعكس. ومتى وجد أحد هذين الأمرين وجد ما به يتميز الذات عن الغير وبالعكس. ( فافهم هذا الذي ذكرناه من معاني الوجوب، وليكن هذا على ذكر منك ) فإنه ينفعك ( فيما يرد عليك من أحكامه ) أي أحكام الوجوب من كونه وجودياً أو عدمياً وكونه عين الذات أو زائدا عليها فالمعنى الأول عدمي والأخيران وجوديان بمعنى أنه لا سلب في مفهومهما والثالث عين الذات بخلاف الأولين (وكذا الإمكان) يقال
قوله: (فإما بتأويل الواجب إلخ) إذ ليس الوجوب بذلك المعنى قائماً بذاته تعالى حتى يوصف بما يشتق منه بل هو محمول عليه مواطأة فلا بد من تأويل الوجود بالواجب على التسامح المشهور من ذكر المشتق منه وإرادة المشتق أو يراد بالوجوب مبدؤه على طريق ذكر المسبب وإرادة السبب وعلى التقديرين يكون الوجوب عبارة كون الشيء بحيث يمتاز عن غيره، فتدبر فإنه مما زل فيه إقدام .
قوله : ( لكنها متغايرة في المفهوم والتلازم لا يستلزم التغاير في المفهوم حتى لا الاستدراك على ما وهم لتحقق التلازم مع التغاير بالاعتبار كما في الحد والمحدود. قوله : ( فلأنه إلخ ) فالتلازم بينهما باعتبار التحقق .
قوله: (فيما يرد عليك سواء كان مذكوراً في هذا الكتاب أولا، فلا يرد أن الوجودي والعدمي بالمعنى الذي ذكره الشارح قدس سره ليس مذكوراً في الكتاب، إنما المذكور بمعنى الموجود والمعدوم وهو ليس متفرعا على اختلاف المعاني .
قوله : ( والثالث عين الذات أي صدقاً بخلاف الأولين فإنهما يغايرانه صدقاً وإن كانا عين الذات خارجاً بمعنى أنهما ليسا زائدين عليه في الخارج. قوله : ( وكذا الإمكان إلخ وكذا الامتناع إلا أنه لا كمال في معرفة أحواله، فلذا ترك بيانه .
يسلم بمعنى الصدق عليه، ولك أن تقول : إطلاق الوجوب على المعنى الثالث اصطلاح الفلاسفة النافين للصفات، وأما المعنيان الأولان للوجوب فخروجهما إما تحمل الشيء على الموجود مجازاً أو بحصر سببية لامتيازية في الشيء المستفاد من القديم به مريداً بالامتياز الامتياز الذاتي فتأمل.
قوله : (لكنها متغايرة فإن قلت : التلازم يقتضي التغاير بدون العكس فلا حاجة لقوله أمور متلازمة لكنها متغايرة قلت : كأنه لاحظ أن التلازم يكفيه التغاير الاعتباري كما بين الحد والمحدود ومراده هاهنا التغاير الذاتي، فلذا صرح بالتغاير بعد الحكم باللازم، نعم لو قال متغايرة متلازمة كما ذكره الشارح في معاني الإمكان لكان أظهر.
قوله : ( وكذا الإمكان قيل وكذا الامتناع يدل على الممتنع باعتبار ما له من الخواص
And know that wujub is said of the Necessary Being in consideration of its properties, which are three: The first is its independence (in its existence) from other than it, and it has been expressed by its not needing or its not depending in its existence on other than it. The second: that its essence is what necessitates its existence, a complete necessitation. The third: the thing by which the essence is distinguished from other than it. And applying wujub to the first two meanings is apparent and well-known. As for applying it to the third, it is either by interpreting 'the Necessary Being' or intending the source of wujub.
He said: (And know that wujub etc.) Meaning that wujub in the essential sense is the modality of the relation of existence, so it is an attribute of the relation, and His essence (exalted) is not described by it, otherwise it would be a description by a state of something related. Rather, He is described by it only in consideration of its usage in one of the three meanings that are specific to His essence, because these concepts are necessary to that meaning which is the attribute of the relation, either metaphorically or by homonymy.
He said: (The thing which etc.) That is, this concept in order to be correct as a property specific to Him (exalted), and therefore he added the word 'thing'. And by 'other than it' is meant everything that is other than Him, even His attributes. And that thing is nothing but His personal essence, so this meaning does not apply to other than Him at all. So what is said that it applies to His attributes (exalted) is pure illusion, and likewise in the case of imkan.
He said: (Apparent and well-known, and no doubt in describing His essence (exalted) by wujub in these two meanings by derivation because they are subsisting in His essence.
He said: (And know that wujub is said of the wajib) that is, it is applied to it by derivation, so it is said: God (exalted) is wajib or possesses wujub, i.e., possesses independence in His existence from other than Him, and so on.
He said: (The third: the thing which etc.) It was said: This is more general than the first two because it applies to them and to other than them from the essence itself and from all the other attributes specific to Him (exalted), unless what is meant by 'thing' is existent. And the distinction of the essence by the essence does not impair the statement of its distinction by the attribute also. So that the third property being identical to the essence is only...
(And they) i.e., these properties (are mutually implying things but different in concept). As for their difference, it is because the third property is identical to the essence, for He (exalted) is distinguished by His essence from all that is other than Him; the second is the relation of the essence and existence; and the first is a negative relation consequent upon the positive relation. As for their mutual implication, it is because if His essence is sufficient in necessitating His existence, it does not need in its existence other than it, and vice versa. And whenever one of these two matters is found, what distinguishes the essence from other than it is found, and vice versa. (So understand what we have mentioned of the meanings of wujub, and let this be on your mind) for it will benefit you (in what comes to you of its rulings), i.e., the rulings of wujub, such as whether it is existential or non-existential, and whether it is identical to the essence or additional. So the first meaning is non-existential, and the last two are existential, meaning that there is no negation in their concept. And the third is identical to the essence, unlike the first two. (And likewise imkan) is said.
He said: (For either by interpreting 'the wajib' etc.) For wujub in that sense is not subsisting in His essence (exalted) such that He is described by what is derived from it; rather, it is predicated upon it by conformity. So it is necessary to interpret 'existence' as 'the wajib' according to the well-known license of mentioning the noun from which something is derived and intending the derived term, or what is meant by wujub is its source, by way of mentioning the effect and intending the cause. On both estimations, wujub becomes the expression of the thing being such that it is distinguished from other than it. So contemplate, for it is something in which feet have slipped.
He said: (But they are different in concept, and mutual implication does not entail difference in concept, so that there is no) correction of what was imagined, because mutual implication can coexist with difference by consideration, as in the case of definition and definiendum.
He said: (For because etc.) So the mutual implication between them is in terms of realization.
He said: (In what comes to you, whether it is mentioned in this book or not, so it is not objected that the existential and non-existential in the sense mentioned by the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) are not mentioned in the book. What is mentioned is in the sense of existent and non-existent, which is not a branch of the difference of meanings.
He said: (And the third is identical to the essence) meaning in truth [literally: in truth], unlike the first two, for they differ from it in truth, even though they are identical to the essence externally, meaning that they are not additional to it in external reality.
He said: (And likewise imkan etc.) And likewise imtina', except that there is no completeness in knowing its states, so its explanation was left.
It is accepted in the sense of being true of it. But you may say: The application of wujub to the third meaning is the terminology of the philosophers who negate the attributes. As for the first two meanings of wujub, their being applied is either by carrying the thing upon the existent metaphorically, or by restricting causality for distinctiveness in the thing derived from the eternal, intending by distinctiveness the essential distinctiveness, so contemplate.
He said: (But they are different. If you say: Mutual implication necessitates difference without the converse, so there is no need for his saying 'things mutually implying but different'. I say: It is as if he noticed that mutual implication suffices for conceptual difference as between definition and definiendum, and his intention here is essential difference, so he explicitly mentioned difference after the judgment of implication. Yes, if he had said 'different, mutually implying' as the commentator mentioned in the meanings of imkan, it would have been more apparent.
He said: (And likewise imkan) it was said: And likewise imtina' indicates the impossible in consideration of its properties.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the three properties (khawass) of wujub in relation to the Necessary Being (al-wajib). It begins with the matn statement that wujub is said of the wajib in terms of its three properties: (1) independence from others in existence, (2) the essence itself necessitates existence completely, and (3) the thing by which the essence is distinguished from others. The first two are well-known, while the third requires interpretation. The commentary then explains that wujub in the essential sense is an attribute of the relation of existence, not directly of God's essence; rather, God is described by wujub through one of these three meanings. The first two meanings are applied to God by derivation (ishtiqaq) – e.g., 'God is wajib' meaning He is independent. The third meaning is more subtle: it is either a metaphorical application of 'wajib' to mean the thing that possesses the property of distinction, or it refers to the source of wujub. The passage then discusses the mutual implication (talazum) among the three properties: they are mutually implying but distinct in concept (mutaghayira fi al-mafhum). The third property is the essence itself, the second is the relation of essence to existence, and the first is a negative relation dependent on the positive one. The mutual implication is explained: if the essence is sufficient for existence, then it does not need others, and vice versa. Also, if either of the first two properties holds, the distinguishing property follows. The passage concludes with advice to remember this for rulings on wujub – e.g., whether the first property is non-existential ('adami) while the others are existential (wujudi), and whether the third is identical to the essence (ayn al-dhat) while the first two are not, though they are not additional to the essence externally. Finally, the same analysis applies to imkan (possibility) and imtina' (impossibility), but the latter is less important.

Key Terms
التلازم (al-talazum)
التغاير (al-taghayur)
العدمي ('adami)
الوجودي (wujudi)
عين الذات (ayn al-dhat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the three properties are completely independent of each other.
Correction: The passage emphasizes they are mutually implying (mutalazima) but different in concept.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the third property (distinction) is described as:
A) An added attribute
B) A negative relation
C) Identical to the essence
D) The same as the first property

Key Takeaway
The properties of wujub are mutually implying but conceptually distinct, with the third being the essence itself, and they inform whether wujub is existential or non-existential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The first property of wujub is 'non-existential'—it is a negation of need. In what area of your life do you act as though you are self-sufficient, and how does that contradict the first property's insistence that Allah alone is independent? What will you do today to affirm your utter need for Him?
?
If Allah's distinction from all else is identical to His essence, then your existence is entirely distinct from His. How does that realization change the way you approach your identity? Do you live as if your identity is separate from the world's, or do you blend in? What one action today will express that distinction in your character?
?
The passage says mutual implication: independence implies self-sufficiency and distinction. If you truly internalized that Allah needs nothing and is utterly distinct, what would you stop worrying about? What would you start depending on Him for? Write down one specific fear you will surrender based on this lesson.

Divine Attributes
advanced
10 min
Objection of Infinite Regress from the Necessity of Necessity and Its Answer
Sanusi presents the infinite regress objection and gives a two-part answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection of infinite regress against the necessity of the Necessary Being is answered by appealing to identity or considerational attributes.

Core Idea
The necessity of the Necessary Being does not cause infinite regress because it is identical to Him or merely conceptual.

This lesson presents a key objection in kalam theology: if the attribute of necessity is real, it would require another necessity ad infinitum. The answer, rooted in the identity of attributes or their mental existence, preserves divine simplicity and avoids regress. Sanusi explains the two-part answer and defends it against further objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the dilemma
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the initial dilemma: if necessity is not real, the Necessary Being is not necessary; if it is real, it leads to infinite regress.
The dilemma forces a choice between two problematic outcomes.
2
Understand the first answer: identity of necessity
The first part of the answer claims that the necessity of the necessity is identical to the necessity itself, analogous to the identity of existence and existent. This stops regress without positing a real additional attribute.
This is a direct denial of real multiplicity.
3
Understand the second answer: considerational ranks
The second part allows that ranks of necessity could be merely mental considerations (i'tibārī). The existence of one individual of a nature does not require all individuals to exist, so regress is only conceptual.
Mental considerations do not entail real infinity.

المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثاني : أمور اعتبارية لا وجود لها في الخارج
الوجوب به لم يكن واجباً أصلاً، فبالأولى أن يكون الواجب (ممكناً)، هذا خلف. (وإن كان) الوجوب ( واجباً كان له وجوب ) آخر ( وتسلسل، وجوابه) : أنا نختار الشق الثاني ونمنع لزوم التسلسل إذ ( قد يكون وجوب الوجوب نفسه ) على قياس ما قيل من أن وجود الوجود عينه، وأيضا جاز أن يكون وجوب الوجوب أو ما بعده من المراتب أمراً اعتبارياً، فإن وجود فرد من أفراد طبيعة لا يستلزم وجود جميعها، ولعل هذا هو
تعالى، والمعلول لا يكون سبباً ومحتاجاً إليه للعلة، وإن أراد الملابسة فمسلم، لكنه لا يستلزم إمكانه تعالى لعدم الاحتياج إليه . قوله : (فبالأولى أن يكون ممكناً لاحتياجه إلى الممكن فيكون ممكناً في نفسه وبالنظر إلى علته بخلاف المحتاج إلى الواجب فإنه واجب بالنظر إلى العلة .
قوله: (وإن كان واجباً إلخ) ولا يلزم تعدد الواجب بالذات؛ لأن وجوده في نفسه هو وجوده في ذاته تعالى على ما هو التحقيق من أن وجود الصفة في نفسها هو وجودها في المحل، فيكون وجوده في ذاته تعالى مقتضى ذاته ولا يضر ذلك في انحصار الموجود في الواجب
والممكن، فتدبر.
قوله : ( وجوب الوجوب نفسه بأن تكون الثمرة التي تترتب على الاتصاف بالوجوب
مترتبة على نفسه، فلا يكون زائداً على ذاته على قياس ما قالوا في عينية الصفات والوجود . قوله : ( أمراً اعتبارياً ) أي زائداً على ذات الوجوب متصفاً به کاتصاف زيد بالعمى . قوله : (فإن وجود إلخ هذا مسلم لكن الاتصاف بكل فرد منه يستلزم وجود ذلك الفرد، لأنه حينئذ يكون من الصفات العينية أي مما شأنه الوجود الخارجي، والاتصاف بها فرع وجودها
لكن يتوقف على أن وجود مفهوم يقتضي وجود جميع أفراده وإن بني الكلام على مذهب المتكلمين من أن الكل كيفية للنسب المستحيل الوجود، فالعدمية ظاهرة، والتعليل بعدم البناء
فتأمل .
قوله : ( وجوابه أنا نختار الشق الثاني إلخ هذا جواب جدلي، والمقصود دفع ما أورد على هذا الشق، وإلا فكون الوجوب القائم بالواجب واجباً بالذات مما لا يقبل، كيف وتعدد الواجب بذاته مما لا قائل به والبرهان دل على امتناعه كما سيجيء. وبهذا يندفع ما يقال على قوله : فإن وجود فرد من أفراد طبيعة لا يستلزم وجود جميعها من أن هذا مما لا يشك فيه ولا ينكره أحد، إلا أن هذا القدر لا يفيد في هذا المقام، بل المهم هاهنا بیان جواز اتصاف فرد موجود من طبيعة بفرد معدوم منها، مع أنه لم يوجد في أفراد كلي هذا الاتصاف قط فتدبر. قوله : ( ما بعده من المراتب أمراً اعتبارياً) إن حمل الاعتباري على المعدوم في الخارج فإنه يكفي . سند المنع لزوم التسلسل فالأمر ظاهر وإن حمل على الممتنع لم يستقم في أفراد طبيعة نوعية إلا عند المتكلمين وقدمت الإشارة إليه في المتن في أواخر المقصد الحادي عشر من مقاصد الماهية، حيث قلنا : دليل الحكماء على أنه ليس للواجب تعالى ماهية كلية .
قوله : ( ولعل هذا هو المراد) فمعنى كون وجوب الوجوب نفسه أنه ليس زائداً عليه في الخارج، وبهذا يندفع ما يقال لو كان وجوب الوجوب نفسه لكان محمولاً عليه بالمواطأة ضرورة، واللازم باطل لأن الوجوب إذا كان واجباً كان حمل الوجوب عليه بالاشتقاق دون المواطأة، إذ لا معنى للواجب إلا ماله الوجوب، على أنا نمنع بطلان الحمل بالمواطأة، والحمل بالاشتقاق لا ينافيه ألا يرى أن الوجود إذا كان موجوداً بوجود هو نفسه كما ادعاه البعض يصدق عليه أنه وجود وموجود وكذا الوجوب
The third observatory - the second objective: Considerational matters that have no existence in the external world. The necessity (wujūb) by which [the necessary being] would not be necessary at all, so a fortiori the necessary being would be possible (mumkin), which is a contradiction. And if the necessity is necessary, then it would have another necessity and an infinite regress (tasalsul). And its answer: We choose the second alternative and we deny the necessity of infinite regress, since the necessity of the necessity may be itself, analogously to what was said that the existence of existence is identical to it, and also it is possible that the necessity of the necessity or what is after it of the ranks is a considerational matter (amr i'tibārī), for the existence of an individual of a nature does not entail the existence of all its individuals, and perhaps this is what is meant. And the effect cannot be a cause and in need of the cause, and if he intended connection (mulābasa) it is granted, but it does not entail possibility of Him exalted due to lack of need for it. His statement: 'so a fortiori it would be possible due to its need for the possible, so it would be possible in itself and in relation to its cause, unlike the one in need of the necessary, for it is necessary in relation to the cause.' His statement: 'And if it is necessary, etc.' And it does not entail multiplicity of the necessary in essence, because its existence in itself is its existence in His essence exalted, according to the verification that the existence of the attribute in itself is its existence in the subject, so its existence in His essence exalted is required by His essence, and that does not harm the limitation of existing to the necessary and the possible, so reflect. His statement: 'The necessity of the necessity itself, such that the fruit that follows from being described by necessity follows from itself, so it is not additional to its essence, analogously to what they said about the identity of attributes and existence.' His statement: 'A considerational matter' i.e., additional to the essence of necessity, described by it like the description of Zayd by blindness. His statement: 'For the existence, etc.' This is granted, but the description by each individual of it entails the existence of that individual, because at that time it would be among the real attributes, i.e., those whose nature is external existence, and description by them is a branch of their existence, but it depends on [the claim] that the existence of a concept entails the existence of all its individuals, even if the discussion is built on the school of the theologians that the whole is a quality of relations impossible of existence, so nothingness is apparent, and the explanation by lack of construction, so ponder. His statement: 'And its answer: We choose the second alternative, etc.' This is a dialectical answer, and the purpose is to repel what was objected to this alternative, otherwise that the necessity subsisting in the necessary being is necessary in essence is unacceptable, how can multiplicity of the necessary in essence be something held by anyone, and the demonstration indicates its impossibility as will come. And by this is repelled what is said concerning his statement: 'For the existence of an individual of a nature does not entail the existence of all its individuals' – that this is something not doubted nor denied by anyone, except that this much does not benefit in this context, rather the important here is to state the permissibility of describing an existing individual of a nature by a nonexistent individual of it, while such description has never occurred in the individuals of a universal, so ponder. His statement: 'What is after it of the ranks is a considerational matter' – if considerational is taken to mean nonexistent in the external world, then it suffices as the basis for denying the necessary regress, so the matter is apparent; but if taken to mean impossible, it is not valid for individuals of a specific nature except with the theologians, and reference was made to it in the text at the end of the eleventh objective of the objectives of quiddity, where we said: 'The demonstration of the philosophers that the Necessary Exalted has no universal quiddity.' His statement: 'And perhaps this is what is meant' – so the meaning of the necessity of the necessity being itself is that it is not additional to it in the external world, and by this is repelled what is said: 'If the necessity of the necessity were itself, it would be predicated on it by synonymity necessarily, and the consequent is false because when the necessity is necessary, predication of necessity on it is by derivation (ishtiqāq) not by synonymity (muwāṭa'a), since there is no meaning of 'necessary' except that which has necessity;' but we deny the falsity of predication by synonymity, and predication by derivation does not contradict it; do you not see that if existence is existent by an existence that is itself, as some claim, it is true of it that it is existence and existent, and likewise necessity.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer concerning the nature of the necessity (wujūb) attributed to the Necessary Being (wājib). The argument begins by posing a dilemma: if the necessity by which the Necessary Being is necessary is not a real attribute (i.e., not existent), then the being would not be necessary at all—leading to contradiction. If, on the other hand, the necessity is itself necessary, then it would require another necessity, and so on ad infinitum, resulting in an infinite regress (tasalsul). The answer chooses the second horn (that the necessity is necessary) but denies that regress necessarily follows. Two justifications are offered: first, the necessity of the necessity might be identical to the necessity itself, analogous to the claim that the existence of existence is identical to existence (a doctrine of the identity of attributes). Second, even if the ranks of necessity are multiple, they could be merely considerational (i'tibārī), existing only in the mind; the existence of one individual of a nature does not entail existence of all individuals. The commentary elaborates each point: it explains that the identity of the necessity with itself avoids real multiplicity, and that considerational attributes do not cause real regress. It also addresses a subtle objection: if the necessity of necessity is considerational, does describing an existing individual by a nonexistent attribute make sense? The answer is that such description is possible in the mind, as per the theologians. The passage concludes with a discussion of predication: if the necessity of necessity is itself, it can be predicated by synonymity or derivation, and both are acceptable; indeed, existence itself is predicated of itself in a similar way.

Key Terms
wujūb
wājib
mumkin
tasalsul
i'tibārī
'ayniyya
muwāṭa'a
ishtiqāq

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if the necessity of the Necessary Being is necessary, it creates an actual infinite regress.
Correction: The answer shows this regress is avoided by either identity (the necessity is not additional) or by considerational status (mental existence does not entail real infinity).

Checkpoint
What is the main objection presented in this passage?
A) The Necessary Being cannot have attributes.
B) Necessity attributed to the Necessary Being leads to infinite regress if it is itself necessary.
C) The necessity of the Necessary Being is impossible because it would make the being possible.
D) The theologians deny the existence of attributes.

Key Takeaway
The infinite regress objection is resolved by affirming that the necessity of the Necessary Being is either identical to Him or merely a mental consideration, thus not entailing an actual chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that God's necessity is identical to His essence, does your reliance on Him become more direct and personal, or do you still think of His attributes as separate? How would your daily trust in God change if you truly believed His attributes are not added to Him?
?
The objection of infinite regress is a rational argument. But have you ever caught yourself thinking that God's greatness could be 'too much' or that He must fit into your limited categories? How does this lesson challenge you to submit your mind to the truth that God is beyond any chain of causes?
?
If you really understand that the necessity of God is not a separate thing but is Him, does that make you feel closer to Him or more awe-struck? Imagine standing before Him knowing that His very essence is necessity—does that call you to a more constant state of need and dependence on Him?

The Objection of the Possibility of Necessity and Its Refutation
Presents the objection of possibility and the initial answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of the attribute of necessity does not entail the possibility of the Necessary Being, and how the early refutation establishes the identity of wujūb and wujūbiyya.

Core Idea
A possible attribute does not make its subject possible.

The passage opens with a clarification of what it means for the necessity of the necessity to be itself. An objection arises: if the necessity itself is possible, then the Necessary Being might become possible. The author counters by distinguishing the source of necessity for the essence versus for the attribute itself, and then denies the causal link by asserting the identity of wujūb and wujūbiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sharpness of the objection and the immediacy of the answer.
2
Identify the objection and its answer
Locate the objection that the necessity itself might be possible, and find how the author answers it. The answer involves a distinction between the necessity's relation to the Necessary Being and to itself.
3
Understand the denial of the causal link
The author rejects the statement 'by the necessity the necessary is necessary' because there is no distinction between wujūb and wujūbiyya. Reflect on what this identity means.
The commentary clarifies that identity is in referent, not concept.
4
Reflect on the identity claim
Ask yourself: if wujūb and wujūbiyya are identical, then the necessity cannot be a cause of the being's necessity. This is a key point in Ash'ari theology.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المراد من كون وجوب الوجوب نفسه وإلا لم يصح؛ لأن وجوب الوجوب نسبة، بل كيفية نسبة بين الوجوب ،ووجوده فلا يجوز أن يكون نفسه. وربما نختار الشق الأول. (ويجاب عنه ) أي عن الوجه الأول : ( بأنه قد يكون) الوجوب ( ممكناً ولا يلزم من إمكانه إمكان الواجب ، لجواز أن يكون حصول الوجوب للواجب لذاته، ولا يكون حصول الوجوب لوجوبه لذات الوجوب . وقولك به أي بالوجوب ( يجب الواجب، قلنا : ممنوع لعدم التغاير بين الوجوب وكون الواجب واجباً، ( فإن الواجبية كما أنه فرع وجود الموصوف، لئلا يلزم السفسطة كما هو المذكور في شرح التجريد وحققه المحقق الدواني .
( قوله : وإلا لم يصح إلخ ) فيه بحث لأنه إنما يلزم عدم الصحة لو أريد العينية في المفهوم وأما لو أريد العينية فيما صدقا عليه مع التغاير في المفهوم كما حررناه، فلا كما لا يخفى . قوله : ( أن يكون حصول إلخ) فيكون الوجود ضرورياً له فيكون واجباً .
قوله : ( ولا يكون حصول إلخ) بل يكون حصوله له لذات الواجب تعالى فيكون ممكناً نعم يلزم حينئذ تقدم الواجب تعالى على وجوده ووجوبه وسيجيء بيانه . قوله : ( فإن الواجبية إلخ) سواء أريد بهما المعنى المصدري فتكون النسبة إلى المحل أعني حصوله له والاتصاف به مأخوذاً في مفهومهما، أو أريد بهما الحاصل بالمصدر فتكون النسبة خارجة عنهما، وعلى التقديرين لا يصح القول بأنه لولا قيام الوجوب به لم يكن واجباً؛ لاتحاد الشرط والجزاء. نعم يصح ذلك على تقدير أن يكون الوجوب صفة حقيقية، فتكون النسبة خارجة عنه وتكون الواجبية أمراً اعتبارياً مأخوذاً في مفهومه النسبة، لكنا نقول باتحادهما سواء كانا موجودين أو اعتباريين فاندفع ما قيل : إِن الوجوب على تقدير كونه من الأمور العينية لا يكون عين الواجبية أي كون الشيء واجباً ضرورة مغايرة النسبة لكل من الطرفين، بل يكون الوجوب علة وسبباً لاتصاف الواجب بالوجوب؛ لأن النسبة معلولة لكل واحد من طرفيها، فيلزم أن يكون الواجب في اتصافه بالوجوب مفتقراً إلى أمر ممكن، هذا خلف .
قوله : (قلنا : ممنوع لعدم التغاير) فيه بحث لأن مراد المستدل أن اتصاف الذات بالوجوب سبب الوجوب، والمغايرة فيه ظاهرة .
The meaning of 'the necessity of the necessity being itself' — otherwise it would not be correct, because the necessity of the necessity is a relation, rather a quality of a relation between the necessity and its existence, so it cannot be itself. And perhaps we choose the first alternative. And it is answered concerning the first aspect: that the necessity may be possible, and its possibility does not entail the possibility of the Necessary Being, because it is possible that the occurrence of necessity for the Necessary Being is by itself, and the occurrence of necessity for the necessity is not by the essence of the necessity. And your statement 'by it (i.e., by the necessity) the necessary being is necessary' — we say: it is prevented because there is no distinction (taghāyur) between the necessity (wujūb) and the fact of the necessary being being necessary (wujūbiyya). For the wujūbiyya is a branch of the existence of the described, lest sophistry follow, as mentioned in Sharḥ al-Tajrīd and verified by al-Muḥaqqiq al-Dawānī. (His statement: 'Otherwise it would not be correct, etc.') In it there is discussion, because lack of correctness would only follow if identity ('ayniyya) is intended in concept, whereas if identity is intended in the referent while there is distinction in concept, as we have established, then it does not follow, as is not hidden. His statement: 'That the occurrence, etc.' — then existence would be necessary for it, so it would be necessary. His statement: 'And the occurrence is not, etc.' — rather its occurrence is for it through the essence of the Necessary Exalted, so it would be possible; yes, then it would necessitate the priority of the Necessary Exalted over its existence and its necessity, and its explanation will come. His statement: 'For the wujūbiyya, etc.' — whether by both are meant the infinitive meaning, so the relation to the subject, i.e., its occurrence for it and the description by it, is taken into their concepts, or by both is meant the product of the infinitive, so the relation is external to them; and on both suppositions, it is not correct to say that 'if the necessity did not subsist in it, it would not be necessary' because of the identity of condition and result. Yes, that is correct on the supposition that the necessity is a real attribute (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya), so the relation is external to it and the wujūbiyya is a considerational matter in whose concept the relation is taken; but we say they are identical whether they are existent or considerational, so what is said is repelled: that if the necessity is among real matters, it is not identical to wujūbiyya, i.e., the thing being necessary, because of the necessary distinction of the relation from each of the two sides; rather the necessity is the cause and reason for the description of the necessary being by necessity, because the relation is an effect of each of its two sides, so it would follow that the necessary being, in its description by necessity, is in need of a possible matter — this is a contradiction. His statement: 'We said: prevention due to lack of distinction' — in it there is discussion, because the objector intends that the description of the essence by necessity is the cause of the necessity, and the distinction is apparent in it.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the nature of the necessity (wujūb) of the Necessary Being. It begins by questioning the meaning of 'the necessity of the necessity being itself' – if it means real identity, it is problematic because necessity of necessity is a relation, so cannot be identical to the necessity itself. Therefore, one might choose the first alternative, i.e., that the necessity is possible (mumkin). The answer to this objection is then given: even if the necessity is possible, this does not entail that the Necessary Being (wājib) is possible, because the necessity might attach to the Necessary Being by its very essence, while the attachment of necessity to the necessity itself is not by the essence of the necessity. Thus, the Necessary Being remains necessary in itself. The passage then addresses the claim that 'by the necessity the necessary being is necessary' – this is denied because there is no distinction (taghāyur) between the necessity (wujūb) and the state of being necessary (wujūbiyya). The wujūbiyya is a branch of the existence of the subject, lest one fall into sophistry. The commentary elaborates on the identity of wujūb and wujūbiyya: if identity is intended in the referent (i.e., both denote the same reality) while the concepts differ, then the objection fails. The passage also considers two possible interpretations of wujūb and wujūbiyya—whether they refer to the infinitive (maṣdarī) or the product (ḥāṣil bi al-maṣdar)—and concludes that in both cases the conditional statement 'if not for the necessity, the Necessary would not be necessary' is invalid because the condition and result are identical. Only if necessity is a real attribute (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya) does the statement become meaningful, but then the necessity would be a cause for wujūbiyya, leading to a regress in which the Necessary relies on a possible. The author holds that wujūb and wujūbiyya are identical, whether existent or considerational, thus avoiding the objection. The final note points out that the objector's argument assumes a distinction between the essence and the attribute, but this is precisely what is being debated.

Key Terms
wujūb
wujūbiyya
mumkin
wājib
taghāyur
'ayniyya

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The possibility of the attribute of necessity makes the Necessary Being itself possible.
Correction: The attribute's possibility does not transfer to the essence because the attribute may be necessary for the essence by the essence itself.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the statement 'by the necessity the necessary being is necessary'?
A) Because the necessity is not a real attribute.
B) Because there is no distinction between wujūb and wujūbiyya.
C) Because the necessity is itself necessary.
D) Because the Necessary Being does not need necessity.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of the attribute of necessity does not imply the possibility of the Necessary Being; moreover, wujūb and wujūbiyya are identical, so necessity does not cause the being to be necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's attributes—like His power or knowledge—do you ever treat them as if they are separate 'things' added to God? This lesson shows that the necessity attributed to God is identical to God's being. How might you be guilty of mentally dividing God? What would it take for you to truly worship God as one, without compartmentalizing His attributes?
?
The passage warns against sophistry—using clever arguments to avoid the truth. In your own spiritual life, are there areas where you use intellectual reasoning to delay obedience or justify sin? Will you commit today to examine one such area and submit it to God, even if it doesn't 'make sense' to you?

The Detailed Identity of Wujūb and Wujūbiyya
Elaborates on the identity of wujūb and wujūbiyya through two interpretations and rejects the real attribute alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed arguments showing that wujūb and wujūbiyya are identical in reality, whether considered as infinitive or product, and how the suggestion of a real attribute leads to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Wujūb and wujūbiyya are one reality, not cause and effect.

The previous lesson established the identity claim. Now the commentator elaborates on the two possible interpretations of wujūb and wujūbiyya—as infinitive meanings or as products—and shows that in both cases the identity holds. The passage also examines the alternative that wujūb is a real attribute, which would make wujūbiyya a consideration and create an undesirable regress, thus reinforcing the identity thesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the detailed commentary style.
The passage is denser than the previous; take your time.
2
Understand the two interpretations
The passage presents two ways to understand wujūb and wujūbiyya: as infinitive (maṣdarī) meanings or as products (ḥāṣil bi al-maṣdar). Notice how each affects the relation to the subject.
3
Analyze the real attribute hypothesis
The passage considers what would happen if wujūb were a real attribute (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya). It shows that this would make wujūb a cause of wujūbiyya, leading to a regress.
This is the key argument that reinforces the identity thesis.
4
See how the regress is avoided
The author concludes that wujūb and wujūbiyya are identical, whether they are existent or considerational, thus avoiding the regress.
Reflect on why the identity is necessary to avoid dependence on a possible matter.

The Second Argument: Wujub as Dichotomy and the Verbal Dispute
Second argument that wujub must be identical or additional, leading to verbal dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against the external existence of wujub and why the dispute with opponents is merely verbal.

Core Idea
Wujub cannot be identical to the essence nor additional, so the debate is about definitions.

This lesson continues the critique of wujub as an existing attribute. The author presents a stronger argument based on a dichotomy: either wujub is the essence itself or something additional. After refuting the first option and postponing the second, he considers an opponent's redefinition that turns the dispute into a verbal one. You will see how clarifying terms resolves seemingly deep disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Read the dichotomy and its refutation
Read the Arabic passage carefully and note the two options: wujub identical to essence or additional. Focus on the refutation of identity—why wujub cannot be the essence itself.
The refutation uses the idea that wujub is a relation or quality of a relation, making it posterior to the essence.
2
Understand the opponent's response
The opponent denies that wujub is a relation and chooses identity. Read how the author interprets this: the opponent may mean something else by wujub—distinction rather than necessity.
This shift in meaning is the key to seeing the debate as verbal.
3
Reflect on the verbal dispute
Consider why defining terms carefully matters. The author shows that once the meanings are clarified, the dispute loses its substance.
Think of other theological debates that might be resolved by clarifying definitions.

الوجه الثاني وهو الأقوى أنه لو كان الوجوب موجوداً فإما نفس الماهية، ويبطله أنه نسبة بل كيفية عارضة لنسبة بين الماهية والوجود فيكون متأخراً عن الماهية بمرتبة واحدة بل بمرتبتين فكيف يكون نفسها؟ وإما زائداً على الماهية، وسنبطله حيث نبين أن الوجوب على تقدير كونه موجوداً لم يجز أن يكون زائداً على ماهية الواجب، ولم يتعرض لكونه جزءاً منها لأنه ظاهر البطلان وأيضاً كونه نسبة ينافيه. ومن أجاب عن هذا الوجه الثاني بأن منع كونه نسبة فقال: نختار أنه على تقدير وجوده عين الذات، ولا يمكن حينئذ كونه نسبة فلعله أراد بالوجوب المعنى الثالث أعني ما تتميز به الذات، فإنه تعالى متميز بذاته عن جميع ما عداه، لا بصفة تسمى الوجوب فيكون النزاع لفظياً، لأن المستدل أراد بالوجوب اقتضاء الذات للوجود، والمانع أراد به ما تتميز به الذات عن الغير. وفي الملخص إن أريد بالوجوب عدم توقفه في وجوده على...
The second argument, which is stronger, is that if wujub existed, it would be either the essence itself, and it is refuted that it is a relation, rather an accidental quality of a relation between essence and existence, so it is posterior to the essence by one rank, indeed by two ranks, so how could it be the essence itself? Or it would be additional to the essence, and we will refute it where we show that wujub, on the supposition of its existence, cannot be additional to the essence of the Necessary. And he did not consider the possibility of it being a part because that is obviously false, and also being a relation contradicts it. Some have answered this second argument by denying that it is a relation and saying: we choose that on the supposition of its existence, it is identical to the essence, and then it cannot be a relation. Perhaps he meant by wujub the third meaning, i.e., that by which the essence is distinguished, for He Most High is distinguished by His essence from all others, not by an attribute called wujub. So the dispute becomes verbal, because the proponent of the proof meant by wujub the essence's requiring existence, while the opponent meant by it what distinguishes the essence from others. And in al-Mulakhkhas, if by wujub is meant its not depending in its existence on...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the external existence of wujub. It sets up a dichotomy: either wujub is identical to the essence or additional to it. The author refutes the first horn by showing that wujub is a relation (or a quality of a relation) and thus posterior to the essence in ranking, so it cannot be identical. The second horn is promised to be refuted later. The author also notes that being a part is obviously false. Then an opponent responds by denying that wujub is a relation and asserting that it is identical to the essence. The author suggests that this opponent may mean something different by wujub: not the necessity that requires existence, but the characteristic that distinguishes the necessary being from others. Since the necessary being is distinguished by its essence, not by an attribute, this understanding makes the dispute verbal rather than substantive. The reference to al-Mulakhkhas reinforces this point.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you argue about Allah's attributes, how often do you check whether you and your conversation partner are using the same terms with the same meanings? What would it cost you to humbly clarify definitions first?

The verbal dispute here is resolved by recognizing different definitions. In your own life, are there theological disagreements you hold onto that might actually be resolved by asking 'What do you mean by that word?' What stops you from doing that?

Four Examples of Mental Considerations: Qidam, Huduth, Baqa', and Mawsufiyya
Commentator gives four examples of mental considerations proved by infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributes like eternity, temporality, permanence, and being-described cannot be external realities but are mental considerations, as proven by the impossibility of infinite regress.

Core Idea
Attributes such as eternity and temporality must be mental to avoid absurd infinite regress.

This passage applies a key principle of kalam: if an attribute had external existence, it would lead to an infinite regress. The commentator demonstrates this with four examples: qidam (eternity), huduth (temporality), baqa' (permanence), and mawsufiyya (being-described). Each attribute, if real, would cause a contradiction, proving they are mere mental considerations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four examples
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the names of the four attributes: qidam, huduth, baqa', mawsufiyya.
2
Understand the proof structure for each
For each attribute, the commentator assumes external existence and then derives a contradiction (infinite regress or absurd consequence). Follow the logic for each one.
3
Examine the qualifications and objections
Pay attention to the commentator's qualifications, especially for qidam (restricted to divine eternity) and baqa' (confined to non-temporal permanence).
4
Synthesize the principle
After studying all four, articulate the general principle: any attribute whose external existence leads to infinite regress must be a mental consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيه مرتين مرة على أنه حقيقته ومرة على أنه صفته فإنه يجب أن يكون اعتبارياً لا وجود له في الخارج . ( وإلا لزم التسلسل) في الأمور الخارجية المترتبة الموجودة معاً، ( نحو القدم، فإنه لو وجد ) فرد منه ( لقدم ذلك الفرد وإلا كان ذلك الفرد حادثاً مسبوقاً بالعدم، ولا شك أن القدم صفة لازمة لا يتصور انفكاك موصوفها عنها، فإذا كانت مسبوقة بالعدم، كان الموصوف أيضاً كذلك، فيلزم حدوث القديم، والحدوث : فإنه لو وجد ) فرد منه (لحدث وإلا كان قديماً فالموصوف به أولى بالقدم، فيكون الحادث قديماً . ( والبقاء : فإنه لو وجد لبقي ) وإلا اتصف بالفناء، وإذ كان البقاء فانياً لم يكن الباقي باقياً . ( والموصوفية : فإنها لو وجدت لكانت الماهية موصوفةً بها ) قوله : ( مرة على أنه حقيقته أي تمام ماهية ذلك الفرد محمول عليه مواطأة، ومرة على أنه صفته أي قائمة به أي محمول إليه اشتقاقاً. قوله : ( اعتبارياً لا وجود له في الخارج) صفة كاشفة يفيد أن ليس الاعتباري هاهنا بمعنى الفرضي . قوله : (كان الموصوف أيضاً كذلك بناء على امتناع الاتصاف بالصفة الموجودة قبل وجودها، فلا يرد أنه يجوز أن يكون الموصوف قديماً ومتصفاً بها في الأزل، وإن لم تكن موجودة إذ الاتصاف فرع وجود الموصوف دون وجود الصفة، لكن بقي بحث وهو أنه يجوز أن يكون قبل هذا القدم الحادث قدم آخر حادث، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية في جانب الماضي، فلا يكون الموصوف حادثاً مع حدوث صفة القدم. اللّهم إلا أن يبنى الكلام على بطلان التسلسل في الأمور المتعاقبة على ما ذهب إليه المليون وهذا القدر يكفي للمثال. قوله : ( أولى بالقدم بناء على أن قدم الصفة فرع قدم الموصوف . قوله : ( وإلا لكان ذلك الفرد حادثاً مسبوقاً بالعدم ولا شك إلخ) فيه بحث : لأنه إنما يتم في قدم الواجب المتعالي عن أن يكون محلاً للحوادث، وأما في مثل الفلك فلا، لجواز سبق كل فرد من القدم بفرد آخر منه بلا محذور على نحو ما ذكر في حركات الأفلاك ثم إن قوله : ولا شك إلخ مما لا يحتاج إليه لأن مجرد كونه تعالى محلاً للحوادث باطل إلا أن يراد بيان الاستحالة بوجه آخر أظهر ، اللهم إلا أن يقال : القدم عدم المسبوقية بالعدم أصلا، ولا يتصور فيه بالقياس إلى ذات واحدة تعدد الأفراد كما سيأتي نظيرها في الوجوب، وفي عدم تصوره بالنسبة إلى زمانين منع . قوله : ( والبقاء فإنه لو وجد إلخ هذا لا يجري في بقاء الحادث زمانين كما لا يخفى، إذ لا محذور في فناء الباقي في الزمان الثالث . قوله : ( لكانت الماهية موصوفة بها أي لكانت ماهية الموصوفية موصوفة بالموصوفية بالوجود، إذ لو لم يرد ماهية الموصوفية لم يتكرر النوع بالمعنى المذكور .
It is considered twice: once as its essence and once as its attribute; then it must be a mental consideration with no existence in the external world. (Otherwise an infinite regress would follow) in external things that are ordered and exist together. (For example, Eternity: if an individual of it existed, that individual would be eternal; otherwise that individual would be temporal, preceded by non-existence. And there is no doubt that Eternity is a necessary attribute whose subject cannot be conceived without it. So if it is preceded by non-existence, the subject would also be so, and thus the temporalness of the Eternal would follow. And Temporality: if an individual of it existed, it would be temporal; otherwise it would be eternal, so its subject is more deserving of eternity, and thus the temporal would be eternal. And Permanence: if it existed, it would be permanent; otherwise it would be characterized by passing away. And if Permanence is passing away, then the permanent would not be permanent. And Being-described: if it existed, the essence would be described by it. His statement: 'once as its essence' meaning the complete essence of that individual predicated identically, and 'once as its attribute' meaning subsisting in it, i.e., predicated derivatively. His statement: 'a mental consideration with no existence in the external world' is an explicative attribute indicating that 'mental' here does not mean hypothetical. His statement: 'the subject would also be so' is based on the impossibility of being described by an existing attribute before its existence. So it cannot be objected that the subject could be eternal and described by it in pre-eternity even if the attribute did not exist, because being described is a branch of the subject's existence, not the existence of the attribute. But a remaining discussion: it is possible that before this temporal Eternity there is another temporal Eternity, and so on to infinity in the past, so the subject would not be temporal with the occurrence of the attribute of Eternity—unless the discourse is based on the nullity of infinite regress in successive things as held by the theologians, and this much suffices for an example. His statement: 'more deserving of eternity' is based on the fact that the eternity of the attribute is a branch of the eternity of the subject. His statement: 'otherwise that individual would be temporal preceded by non-existence, and there is no doubt, etc.' contains a discussion: because it only applies to the Eternity of the Necessary, who is exalted above being a locus for temporal events. As for things like the celestial sphere, it does not apply, because it is possible for each individual of Eternity to be preceded by another individual of it without trouble, as mentioned in the motions of the spheres. Moreover, his statement 'and there is no doubt, etc.' is unnecessary because the mere fact that He, exalted, is a locus for temporal events is false, unless it is intended to show the impossibility in another more apparent way. Unless it is said: Eternity is the absence of being preceded by non-existence at all, and it is not conceivable for a single essence to have multiple individuals, as will come with Necessity. And there is a prevention regarding its non-conceivability with respect to two times. His statement: 'and Permanence: if it existed, etc.' does not apply to the permanence of a temporal thing for two times, as is clear, because there is no trouble in the permanent passing away in the third time. His statement: 'the essence would be described by it' means that the essence of being-described would be described by being-described with existence, because if the essence of being-described were not intended, the type would not be repeated in the mentioned sense.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage applies the first principle to four attributes: qidam (eternity), huduth (temporality), baqa' (permanence), and mawsufiyya (being-described). The commentator shows that each must be a mental consideration because if it had external existence, an infinite regress would follow. For qidam: if an individual of qidam existed, that individual would be eternal; otherwise it would be temporal, but since qidam is a necessary attribute, its being temporal would imply that the eternal (Allah) is temporal—an absurdity. For huduth: if it existed, it would be temporal; otherwise eternal, leading to the temporal being eternal. For baqa': if it existed, it would be permanent; otherwise it would be characterized by passing away, contradicting permanence. For mawsufiyya: if it existed, the essence would be described by it, but that would require another description, leading to infinite regress. The commentator then addresses objections: the argument for qidam applies only to the Necessary Existent (God), not to celestial spheres where multiple instances of qidam might occur successively; the example of permanence does not apply to temporal permanence lasting only two times; and mawsufiyya is explained as the essence of being-described being described by being-described with existence.

حدوث
بقاء
موصوفية
تسلسل
اعتباري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument regarding qidam (eternity) applies to any eternal being, not just God.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that the argument only applies to the Necessary Existent (God), not to celestial spheres, where multiple individuals of eternity can succeed each other without contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must mawsufiyya (being-described) be a mental consideration?
A) Because it is a necessary attribute of God
B) Because if it existed, it would lead to an infinite regress of descriptions
C) Because it is an accidental attribute
D) Because it has no individuals

Key Takeaway
The attributes of eternity, temporality, permanence, and being-described are mental constructs because their external existence leads to infinite regress or logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After learning that even the attribute of eternity (qidam) is a mental construct to safeguard divine transcendence, how does this challenge your tendency to think you fully understand God's nature? What will you do this week to remind yourself that your concepts of God are limited and must be held with humility?
?
The commentator takes care to limit the argument for qidam to God alone, not to celestial spheres. Have you ever applied a theological principle too broadly, perhaps in a debate or in your own reasoning? What will you change to ensure your speech about God is precise and contextually correct?
?
If 'being described' (mawsufiyya) must be a mental consideration to avoid infinite regress, then every attempt to capture God in words falls short. How will this affect your practice of dhikr (remembrance) and du'a (supplication)? Are you willing to let your words be imperfect, trusting that God knows what you intend beyond your limited descriptions?
