The Seventh Doubt: The Totality of Events and Its Need for a Cause
Sanusi presents the seventh doubt: the totality of events requires a cause, but neither an originated nor an eternal cause is acceptable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh doubt against the Ash'ari position: the argument that the totality of all events, as a whole, requires an external cause, and the two unacceptable consequences if that cause is either originated or eternal.

Core Idea
The totality of events cannot have a cause that is either part of itself or eternal without leading to contradiction.

This passage presents the seventh doubt (shubha) that opponents raise. They argue that the entire collection of events up to now, considered as a single whole, must have a cause. But if that cause is itself an event, it would be part of the whole, contradicting the requirement that the cause be external. If it is eternal, then its influence must be either eternal (making events eternal) or originated (leading to infinite regress). This sets up the problem that the Ash'ari answer must resolve.

Guided Path
1
Understand the doubt about the totality of events
The objector says the whole set of events (jumlat al-hawadith) is undoubtedly originated. Read the first part carefully to see why origination of the whole is claimed.
Notice that the argument uses the origination of each part to argue for the origination of the whole.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The passage presents two possibilities for the cause: either it is itself an event (originated) or it is eternal. Each leads to a contradiction. Find these two cases and understand the objections.
The first horn: if the cause is an event, it must be both inside and outside the totality (contradiction). The second horn: if eternal, its influence is either eternal (implies events eternal) or originated (implies infinite regress).
3
Reflect on the force of the objection
Ask yourself why this is considered a strong objection. The argument seems to leave no option for a cause that is both external and not leading to regress.
This objection targets the Ash'ari claim that all events are created directly by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السابعة : جملة الحوادث) التي وجدت إلى الآن من حيث هي جملة لا شك أنها حادثة أخذت قوله : (جملة الحوادث إلخ) يعني إذا جميع الحوادث الموجودة إلى الآن التي بعضها مجتمعة وبعضها متعاقبة وسواء قلنا بتناهيها أو بعدم تناهيها من حيث إنها جملة بحيث لا يشذ منها واحد فلا شك في حدوثها وإمكانها لأن حدوث الجزء وإمكانه يستلزم حدوث الكل تعلق الإرادة إلى تعلق آخر وهو ممنوع فإن المختار إذا أوجد شيئاً فالمفعول قصداً هو ذلك الشيء فهو يحتاج إلى إرادة ترجحه، وأما تعلق الإرادة فهو وإن كان أثراً لذلك الفاعل لكن لا لذاته بل لذلك الشيء فلا يحتاج فيه إلى إرادة أخرى بل تلك الإرادة إرادة للمراد قصداً ولنفسها تبعاً وهذا كما أن الموجب إذا أوجب شيئا لا يحتاج في الاتصاف بالإيجاب إلى إيجاب آخر. هذا غاية ما قيل والحق إن عدم الاحتياج إلى إرادة أخرى ظاهر وأما عدم الاحتياج إلى تعلق آخر فمحل بحث للعلم الضروري بأن تعلق الإرادة لا يدخل في علة نفسه، وإلا لزم توقف الشيء على نفسه، فتدبر. قوله : (نقلنا الكلام إلخ إن قيل : هذا الكلام منقوض بالواقعات، كما في قصة الشبع والجوع والعطش. قلنا، سيجيء أن في الكل مرجحاً. قوله : ( فيلزم حينئذ التسلسل في التعلقات إن بني بطلانه على عدم جواز التسلسل في الاعتبارية النفس الأمرية لجريان برهان التطبيق، فلا نسلم ذلك كما تحققته فيما سبق. وإنما يجري البرهان إذا كان للتعلقات وجودات إما في الخارج، أو في العقل، لامتناع الانطباق فيما لم يوجد أصلاً. واتصاف المحل بها لا يستلزم كونها موجودة بأحد الوجودين كما مر . وإن بني على أمر آخر فليبين ذلك ؛ إذ لا نسلم عدم جواز تحقق تعلقات غير متناهية بأن يكون كل تعلق سابق معداً للاحق، فتأمل. وممكنة، فلو كان الحدوث أو الإمكان محوجاً إلى المؤثر لكان لتلك الجملة علة، لكن ( لا) علة لها وإلا فإما حادثة فتكون تلك العلة ( داخلة في الجملة) الشاملة لجميع الحوادث بحيث لا يشذ عنها شيء منها، (وهي) أي تلك العلة (خارجة عنها )؛ لأن المؤثر في الجملة لا بد أن يكون خارجاً عن الأثر فتكون داخلة وخارجة معا، وهذا خلف . ( وإما قديمة فصدورها لا لمؤثر إذ لا يجوز أن يؤثر ذلك القديم فيها، لأن تأثيره فيها إن كان قديماً لزم قدم الحوادث، إذ لا يعقل تأثير حقيقي بلا حصول أثر ، وإن كان حادثاً لزم أن يتصف القديم بصفة متجددة هي المؤثرية، فتكون محتاجة إلى مؤثرية أخرى فننقل الكلام إليها فيلزم التسلسل . ( والجواب : أنها ) أي المؤثرية صفة ( ذهنية) ( فنختار أن المؤثر في جملة الحوادث قديم، وأن له تأثيراً متجدداً، لكنه صفة ذهنية اعتبارية يتصف بها القديم من غير حاجة إلى تأثير آخر، فلا يتسلسل ولقائل أن يقول : الاتصاف بحادث وإن كان عدمياً محتاج إلى مرجح مخصص، فإن قيل : الإرادة كافية في ذلك، قلنا قد مر آنفاً وجه الإشكال فيها . الشبهة وإمكانه، وفي أن حدوثها وإمكانها غير حدوث الجزء وإمكانه؛ لأن حدوث كل جزء وإمكانه يستلزم حدوث الكل وإمكانه ، ولا يستلزم حدوث الجزء الآخر وإمكانه . قوله : ( لأن المؤثر في الجملة أي في جملة الحوادث، فلا يرد النقض بالمجموع المركب من الواجب والحادث، فإن علته ليست خارجة عنه . قوله : ( لا بد أن يكون إلخ إذ لا يجوز أن يكون نفسه للزوم تقدم الشيء على نفسه، ولا جزءه للزوم أن لا يكون مؤثراً في الجملة، بل في بعضها لعدم تأثيره في نفسه، هذا خلف قوله : (فصدورها لا لمؤثر) فلا يكون ما فرضناه علة علة والظاهر فوجودها إذ لا صدور حينئذ قوله : (إذ لا يعقل تأثير حقيقي قيد بذلك؛ لأن التأثير الغير الحقيقي بأن يراد به مبدأ التأثير يعقل وجوده بلا أثر كما قالوا بقدم التكوين مع حدوث المكون . قوله : ( لا شك أنها حادثة وممكنة الحوادث إما مجتمعة أو متعاقبة، وفي المتعاقبة لا يجوز أن يكون السابق معداً للاحق؛ لوجوب اجتماع المعلول مع العلة، فالمؤثر إما حادث مجتمع أو قديم ففي الثاني الأمر ظاهر، وفي الأول ينقل الكلام إلى مؤثره، حتى يوجد جملة حادثة مجتمعة . وبهذا يظهر أن الكلام في الحوادث المجتمعة، فيصح قوله : لا شك أنها حادثة وظهر سر تقرير الشارح الجواب على الوجه المسطور وعدم إرجاعه الضمير في قوله : والجواب أنها ذهنية إلى الجملة قوله : ( إن كان قديماً لزم قدم الحوادث) إذا جوز تقدم التأثير على وجود الأثر آناً لم يزد هذا لأنه قول مرجوع لم يلتفت إليه، وإن نقله فيما سبق .
The seventh doubt: The totality of events that have occurred up to now, considered as a whole, is undoubtedly originated (haditha). I took his words: (the totality of events etc.) meaning that all the events that have occurred up to now, some of them simultaneous and some successive, whether we say they are finite or infinite, insofar as they are a whole from which none is excluded, there is no doubt that they are originated and possible because the origination and possibility of the part necessitate the origination and possibility of the whole. The attachment of the will to another attachment is forbidden, for if the free agent brings something into existence, the intended effect is that thing, so it needs a will that gives it preponderance. As for the attachment of the will, even though it is an effect of that agent, it is not for its essence but for that thing, so it does not need another will; rather, that will is a will for the object of will intentionally and for itself derivatively. This is like how the necessitator, when it necessitates something, does not need another necessitation in being characterized by necessitation. This is the utmost that has been said; the truth is that the lack of need for another will is apparent, but as for the lack of need for another attachment, it is a matter of investigation because necessary knowledge indicates that the attachment of the will does not enter into the cause of itself, otherwise a thing would depend on itself, so reflect. His words: (we transferred the discussion etc.) If it is said: This speech is refuted by actual occurrences, as in the story of satiety, hunger, and thirst. We say: It will come that there is a preponderator in all. His words: (Then in that case an infinite regress in the attachments follows) If its invalidity is based on the non-permissibility of infinite regress in mental things of the self-command due to the running of the proof of application, we do not accept that as you have verified previously. The proof applies only if the attachments have existences either in the external or in the mind, because application is impossible for what does not exist at all. The characterization of the locus by them does not necessitate their being existent in either of the two modes of existence, as has passed. And if it is based on another matter, let it be explained, for we do not accept the non-permissibility of the realization of infinite attachments, each preceding attachment being a preparation for the subsequent one, so reflect. And it is possible, for if origination or possibility requires an efficient cause, then that totality would have a cause, but it has no cause; otherwise it would either be originated, then that cause would be (included in the totality) that encompasses all events such that none is excluded, and (it) meaning that cause is (outside it) because the cause of the whole must be outside the effect, so it would be both inside and outside together, and this is contradictory. Or it would be eternal, then its occurrence is without a cause because it is not permissible for that eternal to affect it; for if its influence in it were eternal, the events would be eternal, since a real effect is inconceivable without an effect occurring; and if it were originated, then the eternal would be characterized by an originated attribute which is influentiality (al-mu'aththiriyya), so it would need another influentiality, and we transfer the discussion to it, leading to infinite regress. (The answer: it) meaning influentiality is a mental attribute (sifa dhihniyya). So we choose that the cause of the totality of events is eternal, and it has a renewed influence, but it is a mental conventional attribute by which the eternal is characterized without needing another influence, so there is no regress. And a questioner may say: The characterization with an originated thing, even if privative, needs a specifying determiner. If it is said: The will is sufficient for that, we say that the aspect of the problem with it has already passed. The doubt and its possibility, and that their origination and possibility are not the same as the origination and possibility of the part, because the origination and possibility of each part necessitate the origination and possibility of the whole, but do not necessitate the origination and possibility of another part. His words: (because the cause of the whole) i.e., the cause of the totality of events, so the objection is not refuted by the composite whole consisting of the Necessary and the originated, for its cause is not outside it. His words: (must be etc.) because it is not permissible for it to be itself, as that would require the thing preceding itself, nor a part of it, as that would require it not being effective in the whole, but only in some of it due to its lack of effect on itself; this is contradictory. His words: (so its occurrence is without a cause) so what we assumed to be a cause is not a cause, and it appears that its existence [is without a cause] since there is no occurrence then. His words: (for a real influence is inconceivable) he qualified with that because non-real influence, meaning the principle of influence, can be conceived to exist without an effect, as they said about the eternity of formation (al-takwin) with the origination of the formed. His words: (there is no doubt that it is originated and possible) The events are either simultaneous or successive. In the successive, it is not permissible for the preceding to be a preparation for the subsequent because of the necessity of the effect coexisting with the cause. So the cause is either an originated simultaneous event or an eternal one. In the second case, the matter is apparent; in the first, the discussion is transferred to its cause until there exists an originated simultaneous whole. By this it appears that the discussion concerns simultaneous events, so his words 'no doubt that it is originated' are correct, and the secret of the commentator's formulation of the answer in the written manner and his not referring the pronoun in his words 'and the answer: it is mental' to the totality becomes clear. His words: (if it were eternal, the events would be eternal) if one permits the precedence of influence over the existence of the effect for an instant, this does not add more, because it is a rejected opinion that is not paid attention to, even if he transmitted it previously.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh doubt (shubha) concerning the totality of events (jumlat al-hawadith). The objector argues that the entire set of events that have occurred up to now, considered as a whole, is undoubtedly originated (haditha) and possible (mumkina). If contingency or possibility requires an efficient cause (mu'aththir), then this totality must have a cause. However, no such cause exists, because if it were something that came into existence, it would be part of the totality (since the totality includes all events without exception), contradicting the requirement that the cause of the whole must be external to it. If it were eternal, then its influence (ta'thir) would be either eternal or originated. If eternal, then the events would be eternal (since a real effect necessarily accompanies the cause); if originated, then the eternal would acquire an originated attribute (al-mu'aththiriyya), leading to infinite regress. The response is that the attribute of influence is mental (dhihniyya) and conventional (i'tibariyya). Thus, we choose that the cause of the totality of events is eternal, and it has a renewed (mutajaddid) influence, but this influence is a mental conventional attribute by which the eternal is characterized without needing another influence, so no regress. A further objection is raised that characterization with an originated attribute, even if privative, requires a specifying determinant (murajjih). The reply is that the will is sufficient, but the earlier discussion about the will already showed the difficulty. The commentator then explains various sub-points: the proof of correspondence (burhan al-tatbiq) does not apply to mental things without existence; the cause must be outside the effect; and the discussion concerns simultaneous events, not successive ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The cause of the totality of events could be a part of the totality itself.
Correction: The cause must be external to the effect; if it were part of the totality, it would be both inside and outside, which is contradictory.

Checkpoint
What is the problem if the cause of the totality is an originated event?
A) It would be eternal, contradicting its origination.
B) It would be both inside and outside the totality (contradiction).
C) It would lead to infinite regress.
D) It would make the events eternal.

Key Takeaway
The total set of events cannot have a cause that is either an event (part of the set) or eternal with a real influence, because each leads to an impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the totality of events in your life, do you truly see them as caused by God's eternal will, or do you sometimes feel that some events are just random or caused by your own efforts? How does this logical argument push you to reconsider that feeling?
?
The objectors used this doubt to deny a creator because they couldn't find a cause that fits. Have you ever rejected a truth because your finite mind couldn't grasp it? What in your life have you dismissed simply because it seemed contradictory to your limited reasoning?
?
If God's influence is eternal and inseparable from His being, then every event is directly from Him. Does that reality make you feel accountable to Him in every moment, or do you still try to distance Him from your daily decisions? What would change if you truly lived as if every breath is a direct act of His causation?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Answer: The Mental Attribute of Influence and the Prevention of Regress
Sanusi gives the answer: the eternal cause has a mental, renewed influence, avoiding regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari response to the seventh doubt: that the influence of the eternal cause is a mental, conventional attribute that does not require another influence, thus avoiding infinite regress.

Core Idea
The influence of the eternal cause is a mental attribute, not a real one, so no regress follows.

Having presented the dilemma, the text now gives the Ash'ari answer. The key move is to distinguish between real influence and mental influence. The eternal cause has a renewed influence (ta'thir mutajaddid), but this influence is an attribute that exists only in the mind (dhihniyya, i'tibariyya). Because it is not a real entity, it does not require another influence, stopping the regress. The passage also addresses a further objection about the need for a specifying determiner.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer carefully
The passage states that the influence (al-mu'aththiriyya) is a mental attribute. Understand why this solves the regress problem.
Because mental attributes do not have real existence, they do not need another cause.
2
Consider the objection about characterization
Someone might say that even a mental characterization with an originated thing requires a determinent. The reply is that the will is sufficient, but the earlier problem with the will is noted.
This shows the depth of the discussion.
3
Relate to the broader argument
Notice how this answer preserves God’s eternal nature while allowing for temporal events through a mental influence.

The seventh doubt: The totality of events that have occurred up to now, considered as a whole, is undoubtedly originated (haditha). I took his words: (the totality of events etc.) meaning that all the events that have occurred up to now, some of them simultaneous and some successive, whether we say they are finite or infinite, insofar as they are a whole from which none is excluded, there is no doubt that they are originated and possible because the origination and possibility of the part necessitate the origination and possibility of the whole. The attachment of the will to another attachment is forbidden, for if the free agent brings something into existence, the intended effect is that thing, so it needs a will that gives it preponderance. As for the attachment of the will, even though it is an effect of that agent, it is not for its essence but for that thing, so it does not need another will; rather, that will is a will for the object of will intentionally and for itself derivatively. This is like how the necessitator, when it necessitates something, does not need another necessitation in being characterized by necessitation. This is the utmost that has been said; the truth is that the lack of need for another will is apparent, but as for the lack of need for another attachment, it is a matter of investigation because necessary knowledge indicates that the attachment of the will does not enter into the cause of itself, otherwise a thing would depend on itself, so reflect. His words: (we transferred the discussion etc.) If it is said: This speech is refuted by actual occurrences, as in the story of satiety, hunger, and thirst. We say: It will come that there is a preponderator in all. His words: (Then in that case an infinite regress in the attachments follows) If its invalidity is based on the non-permissibility of infinite regress in mental things of the self-command due to the running of the proof of application, we do not accept that as you have verified previously. The proof applies only if the attachments have existences either in the external or in the mind, because application is impossible for what does not exist at all. The characterization of the locus by them does not necessitate their being existent in either of the two modes of existence, as has passed. And if it is based on another matter, let it be explained, for we do not accept the non-permissibility of the realization of infinite attachments, each preceding attachment being a preparation for the subsequent one, so reflect. And it is possible, for if origination or possibility requires an efficient cause, then that totality would have a cause, but it has no cause; otherwise it would either be originated, then that cause would be (included in the totality) that encompasses all events such that none is excluded, and (it) meaning that cause is (outside it) because the cause of the whole must be outside the effect, so it would be both inside and outside together, and this is contradictory. Or it would be eternal, then its occurrence is without a cause because it is not permissible for that eternal to affect it; for if its influence in it were eternal, the events would be eternal, since a real effect is inconceivable without an effect occurring; and if it were originated, then the eternal would be characterized by an originated attribute which is influentiality (al-mu'aththiriyya), so it would need another influentiality, and we transfer the discussion to it, leading to infinite regress. (The answer: it) meaning influentiality is a mental attribute (sifa dhihniyya). So we choose that the cause of the totality of events is eternal, and it has a renewed influence, but it is a mental conventional attribute by which the eternal is characterized without needing another influence, so there is no regress. And a questioner may say: The characterization with an originated thing, even if privative, needs a specifying determiner. If it is said: The will is sufficient for that, we say that the aspect of the problem with it has already passed. The doubt and its possibility, and that their origination and possibility are not the same as the origination and possibility of the part, because the origination and possibility of each part necessitate the origination and possibility of the whole, but do not necessitate the origination and possibility of another part. His words: (because the cause of the whole) i.e., the cause of the totality of events, so the objection is not refuted by the composite whole consisting of the Necessary and the originated, for its cause is not outside it. His words: (must be etc.) because it is not permissible for it to be itself, as that would require the thing preceding itself, nor a part of it, as that would require it not being effective in the whole, but only in some of it due to its lack of effect on itself; this is contradictory. His words: (so its occurrence is without a cause) so what we assumed to be a cause is not a cause, and it appears that its existence [is without a cause] since there is no occurrence then. His words: (for a real influence is inconceivable) he qualified with that because non-real influence, meaning the principle of influence, can be conceived to exist without an effect, as they said about the eternity of formation (al-takwin) with the origination of the formed. His words: (there is no doubt that it is originated and possible) The events are either simultaneous or successive. In the successive, it is not permissible for the preceding to be a preparation for the subsequent because of the necessity of the effect coexisting with the cause. So the cause is either an originated simultaneous event or an eternal one. In the second case, the matter is apparent; in the first, the discussion is transferred to its cause until there exists an originated simultaneous whole. By this it appears that the discussion concerns simultaneous events, so his words 'no doubt that it is originated' are correct, and the secret of the commentator's formulation of the answer in the written manner and his not referring the pronoun in his words 'and the answer: it is mental' to the totality becomes clear. His words: (if it were eternal, the events would be eternal) if one permits the precedence of influence over the existence of the effect for an instant, this does not add more, because it is a rejected opinion that is not paid attention to, even if he transmitted it previously.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh doubt (shubha) concerning the totality of events (jumlat al-hawadith). The objector argues that the entire set of events that have occurred up to now, considered as a whole, is undoubtedly originated (haditha) and possible (mumkina). If contingency or possibility requires an efficient cause (mu'aththir), then this totality must have a cause. However, no such cause exists, because if it were something that came into existence, it would be part of the totality (since the totality includes all events without exception), contradicting the requirement that the cause of the whole must be external to it. If it were eternal, then its influence (ta'thir) would be either eternal or originated. If eternal, then the events would be eternal (since a real effect necessarily accompanies the cause); if originated, then the eternal would acquire an originated attribute (al-mu'aththiriyya), leading to infinite regress. The response is that the attribute of influence is mental (dhihniyya) and conventional (i'tibariyya). Thus, we choose that the cause of the totality of events is eternal, and it has a renewed (mutajaddid) influence, but this influence is a mental conventional attribute by which the eternal is characterized without needing another influence, so no regress. A further objection is raised that characterization with an originated attribute, even if privative, requires a specifying determinant (murajjih). The reply is that the will is sufficient, but the earlier discussion about the will already showed the difficulty. The commentator then explains various sub-points: the proof of correspondence (burhan al-tatbiq) does not apply to mental things without existence; the cause must be outside the effect; and the discussion concerns simultaneous events, not successive ones.

Key Terms
صفة ذهنية
تأثير متجدد
اعتبارية
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The influence of the eternal cause must be a real attribute, otherwise it couldn't produce an effect.
Correction: The text explains that the influence is a mental, conventional attribute. Real influence is not required; the cause is characterized by this mental attribute, and the effect is still produced without needing another cause.

Checkpoint
Why does the mental attribute of influence prevent infinite regress?
A) Because it is a real attribute that exists in the external world.
B) Because it is a mental, conventional attribute that does not need another influence.
C) Because it is eternal and unchanging.
D) Because it is a part of the totality of events.

Key Takeaway
The eternal cause has a mental, renewed influence that does not require another influence, stopping the regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you truly believe that every moment of your life is sustained by a God whose influence is not like a physical cause? How does this affect your feeling of dependence on Him right now?
?
Have you ever doubted God's power because you thought He needed a 'cause' to create? This lesson shows that His influence is mental, not real, and therefore not needing another cause. Will you let this truth remove any hesitation in relying on Him today?
?
The concept of 'mental attribute' might seem abstract. But consider: if God's influence were a real attribute like a created thing, it would lead to an infinite chain. Does this not show the depth of God's transcendence? How should this shape your worship and awe of Him?

The Eternal's Independence from the Free Agent
Jurjani explains the first investigation of the Eternal and the agreement on its independence from the free agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first investigation of the Eternal: that theologians and philosophers agree it cannot depend on a free agent, but they differ on its relation to the necessitating agent.

Core Idea
The Eternal's independence from the free agent is agreed; its dependence on the necessitator is not.

In this passage from Jurjani's commentary, we delve into the Fifth Aim concerning the Eternal (al-qadim). The author outlines two investigations, focusing on the first: the relationship between the Eternal and the free agent. This lesson will clarify the agreement between theologians and philosophers on one point, while highlighting their fundamental disagreement on another.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the argument. Note the key terms and the flow of reasoning.
The passage is a commentary, so it includes glosses in parentheses.
2
Identify the two investigations
Locate where the author states there are two investigations. Understand that only the first is detailed here.
3
Understand the agreement
The passage states that both theologians and philosophers agree the Eternal does not depend on a free agent. Note the reason: a free agent's act requires intention, which is concomitant with non-existence.
4
Grasp the disagreement
Recognize that theologians and philosophers diverge on whether the Eternal can depend on a necessitating agent. The philosophers believe God is a necessitator by essence; theologians do not accept that.
This disagreement leads to different conclusions about the eternity of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الخامس : في أبحاث القديم ) في أبحاث القديم وهي أمران ) أي هي راجعة إليهما ، ( أحدهما أنه ( أي القديم ( لا يستند إلى القادر المختار) أي لا يكون أثراً صادراً منه (اتفاقاً) من المتكلمين وغيرهم. والحكماء إنما أسندوه أي القديم الذي هو العالم على رأيهم (إلى الفاعل) الذي هو الله تعالى ( لاعتقادهم أنه تعالى ( موجب بالذات)، لا فاعل بالاختيار، ولو اعتقدوا كونه مختاراً لم يذهبوا إلى قدم العالم المستند إليه. والمتكلمون لوسلموا كونه تعالى موجباً بالذات (لم يمنعوا استناده) أي استناد القديم (إِليه) تعالى. فالحاصل جواز استناده إلى () الفاعل (الموجب اتفاقاً) من الفريقين ( بأن يدوم أثره ) أي أثر الموجب ( بدوام ذاته، فيكون كلاهما استناد أحدهما إلى الآخر، ويمتنع استناده) أي وامتناع استناده (إلى الفاعل المختار اتفاقاً منهما أيضاً؛ ) لأن فعل المختار مسبوق بالقصد إلى الإيجاد ) دون فعل الموجب إذ لا قصد له ( وأنه) أي القصد إلى الإيجاد مقارن للعدم)،
The Fifth Aim: On Investigations of the Eternal. (He said: 'On investigations of the Eternal, and they are two matters.') Meaning they refer back to them (i.e., the two matters). (One of them: that He, i.e., the Eternal, does not depend on the free agent) meaning it is not an effect proceeding from him (by agreement) of the theologians and others. And the philosophers indeed attribute it, i.e., the Eternal which is the world in their view, to the Agent who is God Almighty, due to their belief that He Almighty is a necessitator by essence, not an agent by choice. Had they believed Him to be chosen, they would not have gone to the eternity of the world dependent upon Him. And the theologians, if they had accepted that He Almighty is a necessitator by essence, would not have denied its dependence, i.e., the dependence of the Eternal, upon Him Almighty. So the result is the permissibility of its dependence upon the necessitating agent by agreement of the two groups, because His effect endures with the endurance of His essence. Thus both are the dependence of one on the other. And the impossibility of its dependence upon the free agent is also by agreement of both, because the act of the chosen one is preceded by the intention to bring into existence, unlike the act of the necessitator, for he has no intention. And that, i.e., the intention to bring into existence, is concomitant with non-existence.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the Fifth Aim (al-maqsad al-khamis) concerning investigations of the Eternal (al-qadim). The commentator begins by stating that the investigations are two matters, though the book lists four rulings. The first matter is that the Eternal does not depend on the free agent (al-qadir al-mukhtar) by agreement of the theologians and others. The second matter is that it depends on the necessitating agent (al-mujib bi al-dhat). The commentator then elaborates: the philosophers attribute the Eternal (the world) to God as a necessitating agent because they believe God acts by essence, not by choice. If they thought He was free, they would not hold the world's eternity. Likewise, if theologians accepted God as a necessitator, they would not deny the Eternal's dependence on Him. The conclusion is that both groups agree on two points: (1) it is permissible for the Eternal to depend on the necessitating agent, as His effect endures with His essence, and (2) it is impossible for the Eternal to depend on the free agent, because a free agent's action requires prior intention (qasd) to create, which is concomitant with non-existence, whereas the necessitator has no intention.

Key Terms
قديم qadim
فاعل مختار fa'il mukhtar
موجب بالذات mujib bi al-dhat
قصد qasd

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That theologians and philosophers agree entirely on the Eternal's dependence; they only agree on its impossibility from the free agent, not on its possibility from the necessitating agent.
Correction: The passage shows they agree only on the impossibility from the free agent; they differ on whether it can depend on the necessitating agent, as philosophers affirm it and theologians deny it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do theologians and philosophers agree upon regarding the Eternal?
A) It can depend on both the free and the necessitating agent.
B) It cannot depend on the free agent.
C) It cannot depend on the necessitating agent.
D) It cannot depend on either.

Key Takeaway
The Eternal's independence from the free agent is a point of agreement between theologians and philosophers, but their disagreement on the nature of God's agency leads to different conclusions about the Eternal's relation to the necessitating agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says the free agent's intention is 'concomitant with non-existence.' When you intend to do something, you are aiming at something that does not yet exist. How does this truth about human intention reveal both your limitations and your dignity as a creature made in God's image? Does this move you to rely more on the One whose acts are not preceded by non-existence?
?
Both theologians and philosophers agree that the Eternal does not depend on a free agent. Yet their deeper disagreements about God's nature lead them to different conclusions. Are there points of agreement with people of different beliefs that you dismiss because of deeper disagreements? What would it cost you to first stand on common ground before addressing differences?
?
If God were a mere necessitator (like a cause that must produce an effect), your relationship with Him would be mechanical. How does your belief that God is a free Agent (al-Mukhtar) shape your prayer, repentance, and hope? Does your daily life reflect trust in a God who acts by choice, or do you sometimes treat Him as a predictable machine?

Resolving the Apparent Inconsistency: The Eternal and Its Cause
Addresses how theologians allow an eternal entity to be caused despite the principle that need is due to origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how theologians reconcile the principle that the eternal has no cause with claims that certain eternal attributes (like God's knowledge or states) are caused.

Core Idea
The eternal's need for a cause is about origination; shifting to possibility resolves the paradox.

Theologians commonly hold that need for a cause arises from origination. This would seem to imply that eternal entities cannot have a cause at all. Yet some theologians, like the Ash'ariyya and Mu'tazila, claim that certain eternal attributes are caused. In this passage, the author explains how this is not a contradiction, either by shifting the ground of need to possibility or by showing that the attachment of will to eternal objects does not entail a cause in the usual sense.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundational principle
The first part of the passage states: if the cause of need is origination (or origination plus possibility), then the eternal has absolutely no need for an agent. This is the starting point.
2
Identify the apparent counterexamples
Look at the references to Ash'ariyya and Abu Hashim: they claim God's knowledge is eternal yet based on His knowledge, and that states like 'being knowing' are caused. This seems to conflict with the principle.
The passage says 'then if you say: the state of the Ash'ariyya...' indicating a potential objection.
3
See the resolution
The passage then explains that the objection can be resolved if the theologian descends from considering origination to considering possibility alone as the ground of need. Also, the argument for God's freedom (being free) is preserved because the attachment of will to originated things occurs temporally or in pre-eternity in a way that does not necessitate an eternal effect.
The final part about t'alluq al-irada being originated or valid as correctness not obligation is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن القائل بأن علة الحاجة هي الحدوث وحده، أو مع الإمكان حقه أن يقول، إن القديم لا يستند إلى علة أصلاً، إذ لا حاجة له إلى مؤثر قطعاً، فلا يتصور منه القول بأن القديم يجوز استناده إلى الموجب إلا أن يتنزل من اعتبار الحدوث إلى اعتبار الإمكان وحده. فإن قلت الحال من الأشاعرة زعموا أن عالميته تعالى مستندة إلى علمه، مع كونهما قديمين وأبو هاشم من المعتزلة زعم أن الأحوال الأربعة وهي العالمية والقادرية ... مثبتو قوله : (يجب أن تكون مختاراً لئلا يكون إيجاده بالقصد الذي هو مسبوق بالعدم، ولا يلزم التخلف لأن تعلق الإرادة حادث أو لأنه تعلق في الأزل بوجوده في وقت مخصوص، أو لأن التعلق يقع على سبيل الصحة لا على سبيل الوجوب .
And know that the one who says that the cause of need is origination alone, or along with possibility, ought to say that the eternal does not have a cause at all, since it has absolutely no need for an agent. Thus, it cannot be imagined that he says: the eternal can be attributed to the necessitating, unless he descends from considering origination to considering possibility alone. Then if you say: the state of the Ash'ariyya? they claimed that His knowledge of things is based on His knowledge, while both are eternal; and Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazila claimed that the four states, namely being knowing, being powerful ... affirmers of his statement: (He must be free) lest His bringing into existence be by intent (qasd) which is preceded by non-existence, and no delay is necessary because the attachment of will is originated, or because it attaches in pre-eternity to its existence at a specific time, or because the attachment occurs as correctness not obligation.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: if the theologians hold that need for a cause is solely due to origination, then they should deny any cause for eternal entities. But some theologians (like the Ash'ariyya) and Mu'tazila (like Abu Hashim) claim that certain eternal attributes (e.g., God's knowledge, or states) are caused by something eternal. The passage then explains that the theologians' argument for God's freedom is not undermined, because the attachment of will to originated things occurs temporally or in pre-eternity in a way that does not necessitate eternal effect. The argument also mentions that the attachment of will can be valid without obligation. The text is somewhat fragmented, but the main point is reconciling the principle that the eternal has no cause with specific examples that might seem contradictory.

Correction: The passage shows that the cause of need is not necessarily origination; if possibility is considered, an eternal can have a cause. The Ash'ariyya likely ground need in possibility.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the Ash'ariyya claim that God's knowledge is eternal yet caused?
A) It is a clear contradiction
B) They must have descended from considering origination to considering possibility as the ground of need
C) They reject the principle that the eternal has no cause
D) They use a different definition of cause

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The theologians shifted from origination to possibility to resolve a contradiction. Is there a false assumption you hold about God that you need to 'descend' from? How would your daily trust in Him change if you let go of that assumption?

The Ash'ari Dilemma on Eternal Attributes
Sanusi presents the Ash'ari dilemma of eternal attributes and their initial defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core dilemma faced by Ash'ari theologians when they affirm eternal attributes subsisting in God's essence, and how they defend it by redefining 'eternal' and asserting the non-distinctness of attributes from God's essence.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes force a choice: multiplicity in God or dependence on another.

Sanusi presents the Ash'ari position on divine attributes and immediately identifies a logical tension. If attributes are eternal and distinct, they either make God multiple or require one eternal to depend on another. Both options seem problematic. This lesson unpacks this dilemma and introduces the Ash'ari apologetic strategy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice the author's presentation of the dilemma and the immediate response.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The passage states the Ash'aris are between two options: either making the necessary being multiple or making the eternal dependent on another. Spot why both are problematic.
The first is false, so the second is determined, but that too has a problem.
3
Understand the two key excuses
The author offers two defenses: (1) the state (ḥāl) is not eternal in the usual sense of 'no beginning of existence', (2) God's attributes are not distinct from His essence, so they don't need a cause.
These excuses aim to show that the dilemma does not actually arise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بالقدم إلا أن يغير تفسيره بأنه ما لا أول لثبوته، وبأن صفات الله تعالى ليست مغايرة له فلا استناد لها إلى علة لأن العلة يجب أن تكون مغايرة لمعلولها. قوله : (فهم) أي الأشاعرة دائرة بين الأمرين . قوله : ( لمعلولها، فهذه الأقوال منهم لا تنافي ما يتصور منهم القول بأن القديم لا يستند إلى الموجب وأما أن هذه الأقوال منافية لما قالوا : من أن علة الحاجة هو الحدوث، فبحث آخر وجوابه : أن ذلك القول منهم إنما هو في الموجودات المغايرة لذاته تعالى . قلت : أي لاعلة حاجة له؛ لأن علة الحاجة عندهم هو الحدوث الزماني، إما مستقلاً أو على وجه الشطرية أو الشرطية . قوله : ( ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها لأنها ثابتة منهم بلا تردد ولا ريب والتنزل أن يكون لو كان العلة هي الإمكان فرضاً وتسليماً لأمكن استناد القديم إلى العلة. قوله بأن القديم مالا أول لوجوده المتصف بالقدم والحدوث حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، وقد يوصف به العدم ،فيقال للعدم الغير المسبوق بالوجود قديم، وللمسبوق حادث كذا في شرح المقاصد لكن المبحث هاهنا هو القديم بمعنى ما لا أول لوجوده، فلم يتجه الإشكال المذكور بقي فيه بحث وهو أن الحال كما لا يوصف بالقدم لا يوصف بالحدوث فكيف جوزوا استناده إلى الغير مع أنه لاعلة حاجة فيه، ويمكن أن يقال : علة احتياج الموجودات هي الحدوث لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً . قوله : (إلا أن يغير تفسيره فحينئذ يوصف الحال بالعدم، لكن لا يرد الإشكال حينئذ أيضاً؛ لما أشرنا إليه الآن من أن الحدوث عندهم علة الاحتياج إلى المؤثر الموجد، لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً .
And being living and being existing are explained by a fifth state, which is divinity, and all of them are eternal. And all the Ash'aris claimed that for God Most High there are existing attributes subsisting in His essence, and they are eternal. Thus they are between making the necessary in Himself multiple and making the eternal depend on another. The first is false, so the second is determined. So these statements from them are contradictory to what they had held considering origination, and there is no room for the interpretation of descent in them. I say: It may be excused for that by the fact that the eternal is that which has no beginning of its existence, so the state (ḥāl) is not described as eternity unless one changes its interpretation to that which has no beginning of its subsistence. And because God's attributes are not distinct from Him, so there is no dependence of them on a cause, because the cause must be distinct from its effect. His statement: ('thus they are') i.e. the Ash'aris are between the two matters. His statement: ('to make') if they say it does not depend on a cause. His statement: ('So these statements of theirs are contradictory') so it is established from them the statement of the eternal depending on a cause, contradicting their statement that the cause of need is origination; so how do you say: it cannot be conceived from them the statement of the eternal's dependence on the necessitating cause while they hold origination as the cause? His statement: ('and no room') since these statements are their belief and they correspond to reality, not on the assumption of considering possibility as the cause of need. His statement: ('It may be excused') means that they are not saying in the mentioned statements that the eternal depends on a cause, because the state is not described as eternity, and the attributes depend on His essence and are not distinct from Him, so there is no dependence on a cause, because the cause must be distinct from its effect. So these statements of theirs do not contradict what can be conceived from them that the eternal does not depend on the necessitating cause. As for these statements contradicting what they said that the cause of need is origination, that is another investigation, and its answer is that that statement of theirs is only about existents distinct from His essence. I say: i.e. there is no cause of need for Him, because the cause of need in their view is temporal origination, either independently or on the basis of partitive or conditional. His statement: ('and no room for the interpretation of descent in them') because they are established from them without hesitation or doubt, and descent is that if the cause were possibility hypothetically and conceded, then the dependence of the eternal on a cause would be possible. His statement: that the eternal is that which has no beginning of its existence; being described with eternity and temporality in truth is existence, while the existent [is described] by reference to it, and non-existence may be described with it: so pre-eternal non-existence is said to be eternal, and that preceded by existence is temporal. Such is in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid, but the investigation here is about the eternal in the sense of that which has no beginning of its existence, so the mentioned objection does not apply. There remains a discussion: that the state (ḥāl) as it is not described by eternity, it is not described by temporality, so how did they allow its dependence on another while there is no cause of need in it? And it can be said: the cause of need for existents is origination, not the cause of need absolutely. His statement: ('unless one changes its interpretation' then the state is described by non-existence, but the objection does not arise then either; because we have indicated now that origination in their view is the cause of need for the effective bringer-into-existence, not the cause of need absolutely.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage addresses the Ash'ari position on God's attributes and Mu'tazili theory of states (aḥwāl). It presents the problem: the Ash'aris say God's attributes are eternal and subsist in His essence, which forces a choice between multiple necessary beings (if attributes are independent) or making one eternal depend on another, both problematic. This contradicts their own principle that need arises from origination (ḥudūth). The response is an apology: (1) The state (ḥāl) is not described as eternal in the sense of having no beginning of existence; only if its definition is changed to 'no beginning of subsistence' could it be eternal. (2) God's attributes are not distinct from His essence, so they do not depend on a cause; a cause must be distinct from its effect. Thus, the Ash'ari statements do not entail that the eternal depends on a cause. However, a separate issue remains: the contradiction with the claim that the cause of need is origination. The answer is that this claim applies only to existents distinct from God, not to the attributes. Further, the cause of need for existents is specifically temporal origination, not need absolutely. The passage also clarifies that the investigation here concerns the eternal as that which has no beginning of existence, so an objection based on states (which are not eternal in that sense) does not apply. The discussion concludes by emphasizing that even if one reinterprets 'eternal' to apply to states, the objection still fails because the cause of need is not absolute origination but origination as the cause of need for an effective agent.

Key Terms
حال (ḥāl)
قديم (qadīm)
صفات (ṣifāt)
علة الحاجة (ʿillat al-ḥājah)
حدوث (ḥudūth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Ash'ari attributes are independent eternal entities.
Correction: The passage clarifies that they are not distinct from God and thus do not require a separate cause.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the initial problem with the Ash'ari claim of eternal attributes?
A) They lead to two contradictory options: either multiple necessary beings or one eternal depending on another.
B) They are impossible to conceive.
C) They conflict with the principle of divine simplicity.
D) They are not mentioned in revelation.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari dilemma shows that affirming eternal attributes appears to force a logical contradiction, but it is resolved by redefining 'eternal' and emphasizing the non-distinctness of attributes from God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a theological dilemma that seems to force a contradiction between reason and faith, do you immediately try to rationalize it or do you sit with the discomfort and allow your understanding of God to expand? How does this lesson challenge your approach to intellectual humility before divine mysteries?
?
The Ash'aris were forced to redefine the meaning of 'eternal' to preserve their position. Have you ever held a belief so tightly that you reinterpreted basic concepts to keep it intact? What did that reveal about your attachment to that belief rather than to the truth?
?
The author presents an apology for the Ash'ari view, but it may not convince everyone. When you encounter a difficult doctrine in your own faith, are you more inclined to defend it or to examine whether your own assumptions need correction? What would it cost you to change your mind?

Refining the Defense: Causality and the Scope of Origination
Sanusi elaborates on the Ash'ari defense, addressing the contradiction with origination as cause of need and refining the concept of causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'aris resolve the apparent contradiction between their affirmation of eternal attributes and their principle that need arises from origination, by limiting the principle to existents distinct from God.

Core Idea
The cause of need is origination only for distinct existents, not for God's attributes.

The previous lesson introduced the dilemma and the initial defense. However, a further contradiction remains: if the cause of need is origination (ḥudūth), how can anything eternal depend on a cause? This lesson unpacks the careful distinction made by Ash'ari theologians between attributes (which are not distinct) and other existents (which are distinct), thereby preserving both the eternity of attributes and the principle that need requires origination.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and observe the structure
This passage is a commentary on earlier statements. Note the repeated 'qawluhu' phrases that indicate responses to objections. Follow the logical flow: objection, counter-response, clarification.
2
Identify the two main objections
The passage addresses: (1) the Ash'ari statements seem to imply dependence of the eternal on a cause, contradicting their principle; (2) even if the state is not eternal in one sense, how can it be dependent at all?
These are developed through the commentary.
3
Understand the key distinction
The resolution lies in distinguishing between attributes (which are not distinct from God) and other existents (which are distinct). Only for the latter does origination serve as the cause of need.
This allows the Ash'aris to maintain both positions consistently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحيية والموجودية معللة بحالة خامسة هي الألوهية وكلها قديمة والأشاعرة كافة زعموا أن لله تعالى صفات موجودة قائمة بذاته وهي قديمة فهم بين أن يجعلوا الواجب بالذات متعدداً، وبين أن يجعلوا القديم القديم مستندا إلى الغير، والأول باطل فتعين الثاني. فهذه الأقوال منهم منافية لما ذهبوا إليه من اعتبار الحدوث، ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها قلت : قد يعتذر عن ذلك بأن القديم ما لا أول لوجوده، فالحال لا يوصف بالقدم إلا أن يغير تفسيره بأنه ما لا أول لثبوته، وبأن صفات الله تعالى ليست مغايرة له فلا استناد لها إلى علة لأن العلة يجب أن تكون مغايرة لمعلولها. قوله : (فهم) أي الأشاعرة دائرة بين الأمرين . قوله : ( أن يجعلوا إلخ ) إن قالوا بعدم استنادها إلى علة . قوله : (فهذه الأقوال منهم منافية إلخ) فقد تحقق منهم القول باستناد القديم إلى العلة مع منافاته لقولهم بأن علة الحاجة الحدوث فكيف قلتم : إنه لا يتصور إلخ) يعني أنهم غير قائلين فيما ذكر من الأقوال باستناد القديم إلى العلة، لأن الحال لا يوصف بالقدم والصفات لاستنادها إلى ذاته تعالى وهي ليست مغايرة له لا استناد لها إلى علة لأن العلة يجب أن تكون مغايرة لمعلولها، فهذه الأقوال منهم لا تنافي ما يتصور منهم القول بأن القديم لا يستند إلى الموجب وأما أن هذه الأقوال منافية لما قالوا : من أن علة الحاجة هو الحدوث، فبحث آخر وجوابه : أن ذلك القول منهم إنما هو في الموجودات المغايرة لذاته تعالى . قلت : أي لاعلة حاجة له؛ لأن علة الحاجة عندهم هو الحدوث الزماني، إما مستقلاً أو على وجه الشطرية أو الشرطية . قوله : ( ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها لأنها ثابتة منهم بلا تردد ولا ريب والتنزل أن يكون لو كان العلة هي الإمكان فرضاً وتسليماً لأمكن استناد القديم إلى العلة. قوله بأن القديم مالا أول لوجوده المتصف بالقدم والحدوث حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that God's attributes are not distinct from His essence, so they do not require a cause like created things. But do you live as if God's knowledge, power, and mercy are inseparable from Him? In your prayers, when you ask for mercy, do you picture it as something separate that God gives, or as an expression of His very being? How would your reliance on God change if you truly felt that His attributes are not distant from you?
?
The Ash'aris teach that your originated existence is the very reason you are in constant need of God. You were nothing, then you were created, and every moment you remain dependent on Him. Has this truth ever really humbled you to the point where you feel your entire being is a loan? What would happen if you spent today consciously aware that your next breath is a new origination from God?
?
The passage warns against confusing God's attributes with created qualities. Have you ever imagined God's knowledge as similar to human knowledge, just bigger? Or His power as a mightier version of human strength? If so, in what concrete ways can you train your mind to think of God's attributes as utterly unique and not like created things? Will you commit to one specific thought or phrase you can repeat when you catch yourself anthropomorphizing?

The Ash'ari Dilemma on Eternal Attributes
Presents the Ash'ari dilemma on eternal attributes and its contradiction with their principle of causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari dilemma regarding eternal attributes and why it contradicts their principle of causation.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes force a choice: multiply the necessary being or make the eternal depend on a cause.

This lesson presents a key internal critique of the Ash'ari position on divine attributes. The Ash'aris affirm that God has eternal attributes subsisting in His essence, but this leads to a dilemma: either those attributes are themselves necessary beings (making multiple necessary beings), or they depend on something else. The Ash'aris reject the first, but the second contradicts their own principle that need for a cause arises from temporal origination (ḥudūth). Let's examine how this dilemma is presented and unpacked.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall argument. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a dilemma, a rejection, and a contradiction.
The passage includes both the main text and the commentator's gloss.
2
Identify the two options
The Ash'aris are said to be 'between making the necessary being by essence multiple, and making the eternal depend on another.' Identify these two horns of the dilemma.
3
Understand why the first is rejected
The passage states that the first option is false (bāṭil). Why? Because multiplicity in the necessary being is impossible. So the second option is forced.
This reflects the principle of tawḥīd.
4
Grasp the contradiction
The second option implies the eternal depends on a cause. But the Ash'aris themselves hold that the cause of need is temporal origination (ḥudūth). How can the eternal, which is not temporal, need a cause? This is the contradiction.
The commentator emphasizes that there is no room for interpretation (tanzzul).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الخامس : في أبحاث القديم

والحياة والموجودية معللة بحالة خامسة هي الألوهية وكلها قديمة والأشاعرة كافة زعموا أن لله تعالى صفات موجودة قائمة بذاته وهي قديمة فهم بين أن يجعلوا الواجب بالذات متعدداً، وبين أن يجعلوا القديم مستندا إلى الغير، والأول باطل فتعين الثاني. فهذه الأقوال منهم منافية لما ذهبوا إليه من اعتبار الحدوث، ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها

قوله : (فهم) أي الأشاعرة دائرة بين الأمرين . قوله : ( أن يجعلوا إلخ ) إن قالوا بعدم استنادها إلى علة . قوله : (فهذه الأقوال منهم منافية إلخ) فقد تحقق منهم القول باستناد القديم إلى العلة مع منافاته لقولهم بأن علة الحاجة الحدوث فكيف قلتم : إنه لا يتصور منهم القول باستناد القديم إلى الموجب مع القول بعلية الحدوث. قوله : ( ولا مجال إلخ ) إذ هذه الأقوال معتقدهم وأنها مطابقة للواقع لا على تقدير فرضية اعتبار الإمكان علة الحاجة.
The Third Observatory - The Fifth Goal: On Investigations of the Eternal

Life and existence are premised on a fifth state, which is divinity, and all of them are eternal. All the Ash'aris claim that Allah the Exalted has attributes that exist subsisting in His essence and they are eternal. Thus they are between making the necessary being by essence multiple, and making the eternal depend on another. The first is false, so the second is determined. So these statements from them are contradictory to what they had adopted of considering temporal origination (ḥudūth). And there is no room for interpretation of condescension (tanzzul) in them.

His saying: ("thus they are") i.e., the Ash'aris are circling between two matters.
His saying: ("between making") etc., if they say it is not dependent on a cause.
His saying: ("so these statements from them are contradictory") etc., for they have been established from them saying that the eternal depends on a cause, contradicting their statement that the cause of need is temporal origination. So how can you say: It is not conceivable from them to say that the eternal depends on the necessitating cause (mūjib) with the statement of causality of temporal origination?
His saying: ("and there is no room") etc., because these statements are their belief and that they correspond to reality, not on the assumption of a hypothetical consideration of possibility as the cause of need.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage defines the problem with the Ash'ari position on divine attributes. It begins by stating that life and existence are premised on a fifth state, divinity, and all are eternal. Then it presents the Ash'ari claim that God has attributes existing in His essence, which are eternal. This leads to a dilemma: either multiply the necessary being (by making each attribute a separate necessary being) or make the eternal depend on something else. The first is false, so they are forced to the second. However, this contradicts their own principle that the cause of need (for a creator) is temporal origination (ḥudūth). The commentator explains each part: when the author says "thus they are," it means the Ash'aris are between two options. When he says "between making," it refers to if they deny attributes depend on a cause. The objection is that they have been proven to say that the eternal depends on a cause, which contradicts their claim that ḥudūth is the cause of need. The commentator rhetorically asks how they can claim the eternal does not depend on the necessitating cause while asserting causality of ḥudūth. Finally, he clarifies that "no room for interpretation of condescension" means these statements are their actual belief and correspond to reality, not a hypothetical assumption.

Key Terms
قديم
واجب بالذات
علة الحاجة
حدوث
تنزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari position on eternal attributes is logically consistent.
Correction: The Ash'ari position forces a choice between multiple necessary beings or making the eternal depend on a cause, thereby contradicting their own principle that need for a cause is due to temporal origination.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second option that the Ash'aris are forced to choose?
A) Making the necessary being by essence multiple
B) Making the eternal depend on another
C) Denying the existence of attributes
D) Accepting that attributes are temporal

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari dilemma shows that affirming eternal attributes leads to a contradiction with their principle that need for a cause is due to temporal origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's attributes, do you ever feel a tension between affirming their reality and avoiding multiplicity? How does this dilemma force you to take a side, and what is at stake for your tawheed if you choose either horn?
?
The Ash'aris were caught in a logical trap because they tried to hold two principles without realizing the conflict. Are there beliefs you hold about God that, if traced to their logical conclusions, lead to contradictions? Are you willing to examine them honestly, even if it means revising a cherished view?
?
If you were in the Ash'ari position, would you accept the contradiction or revise your understanding of eternity and causality? Why does your answer matter for your own relationship with the truth?

The Ash'ari Defense: No Causal Dependence for Eternal Attributes
Ash'ari defense that states are not eternal, so no causal dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari theologians defended the view that divine attributes are eternal yet not dependent on a cause by distinguishing attributes as states (aḥwāl) and redefining the cause of need.

Core Idea
Attributes are states, not distinct entities, so no causal dependence.

The Ash'ari position on attributes faced a challenge: if attributes are eternal, do they require a cause? Their defense hinges on the concept of 'state' (ḥāl), which is not eternal and thus not subject to causal need. This lesson unpacks that defense and its key distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the defense passage
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the translation. Notice how the defense starts by clarifying what the Ash'aris are not saying.
The passage is dense; focus on the logic, not every word.
2
Identify the core argument
The defense argues that attributes are states (aḥwāl) and states are not eternal. They also claim the cause of need is temporal origination, not absolute need. Identify these two points.
3
Consider the implications
Ask yourself: How does the concept of 'state' help avoid the problem of attributing a cause to the eternal? What would the critic say? This prepares you for the refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (قد يعتذر عن ذلك إلخ) يعني أنهم غير قائلين فيما ذكر من الأقوال باستناد القديم إلى العلة، لأن الحال لا يوصف بالقدم والصفات لاستنادها إلى ذاته تعالى وهي ليست مغايرة له لا استناد لها إلى علة لأن العلة يجب أن تكون مغايرة لمعلولها، فهذه الأقوال منهم لا تنافي ما يتصور منهم القول بأن القديم لا يستند إلى الموجب وأما أن هذه الأقوال منافية لما قالوا : من أن علة الحاجة هو الحدوث، فبحث آخر وجوابه : أن ذلك القول منهم إنما هو في الموجودات المغايرة لذاته تعالى . قلنا من أنه أي لاعلة حاجة له؛ لأن علة الحاجة عندهم هو الحدوث الزماني، إما مستقلاً أو على وجه الشطرية أو الشرطية . قوله : ( ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها لأنها ثابتة منهم بلا تردد ولا ريب والتنزل أن يكون لو كان العلة هي الإمكان فرضاً وتسليماً لأمكن استناد القديم إلى العلة. قوله بأن القديم مالا أول لوجوده المتصف بالقدم والحدوث حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، وقد يوصف به العدم ،فيقال للعدم الغير المسبوق بالوجود قديم، وللمسبوق حادث كذا في شرح المقاصد لكن المبحث هاهنا هو القديم بمعنى ما لا أول لوجوده، فلم يتجه الإشكال المذكور بقي فيه بحث وهو أن الحال كما لا يوصف بالقدم لا يوصف بالحدوث فكيف جوزوا استناده إلى الغير مع أنه لاعلة حاجة فيه، ويمكن أن يقال : علة احتياج الموجودات هي الحدوث لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً قوله : (إلا أن يغير تفسيره فحينئذ يوصف الحال بالعدم، لكن لا يرد الإشكال حينئذ أيضاً؛ لما أشرنا إليه الآن من أن الحدوث عندهم علة الاحتياج إلى المؤثر الموجد، لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً .

عين المرصد الثالث - المقصد الخامس : في أبحاث القديم الذات ولا غيرها فلا يلزمهم تعدد الواجب ولا تعليل القديم بغيره . وأنت تعلم أن أمثال هذه الاعتذارات أمور لفظية لا معنوية
His saying: ("one may apologize for that") etc., means that they are not, in the statements mentioned, claiming the dependence of the eternal on a cause, because the state (ḥāl) is not described as eternal, and the attributes, due to their dependence on His essence the Exalted and they are not other than Him, have no dependence on a cause, because the cause must be other than its effect. So these statements from them do not contradict what is conceivable from them to say that the eternal does not depend on the necessitating cause (mūjib). As for these statements being contradictory to what they said, that the cause of need is temporal origination, that is another investigation and its answer: that their statement is only regarding existents other than His essence. We said: (he) i.e., it has no cause of need; because the cause of need according to them is temporal ḥudūth, either independently or in the manner of part or condition. His saying: ("and there is no room for interpretation of condescension in them because they are established from them without hesitation or doubt, and the condescension is that if the cause were possibility as a hypothesis and assumption, then the dependence of the eternal on a cause would be possible." His saying that the eternal is that which has no beginning of its existence. What is described by eternity and temporal origination in reality is existence. As for the existent, it is by consideration. And non-existence may be described by it, so it is said to non-existence not preceded by existence: eternal; and to that preceded by existence: originated. Thus in Sharh al-Maqāsid, but the discussion here is about the eternal in the sense of what has no beginning of its existence, so the mentioned objection does not apply. Remaining for discussion is that the state, just as it is not described by eternity, is not described by temporal origination. So how did they permit its dependence on another while it has no cause of need? And it can be said: The cause of need of existents is temporal origination, not the cause of need absolutely. His saying: ("unless one changes its interpretation, then the state would be described by non-existence, but the objection would not apply then either; because of what we have indicated now, that temporal origination according to them is the cause of need for the creating effect, not the cause of need absolutely.")

(The same text from page 186) The essence and not other than it, so they are not forced into multiplicity of the necessary nor making the eternal dependent on another. And you know that such apologies are verbal matters, not conceptual.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents a defense of the Ash'ari position on attributes and its refutation. The defense argues that the Ash'aris are not claiming that the eternal depends on a cause because the 'state' (ḥāl) is not eternal, and the attributes are not other than God, so they have no need of a cause. The commentator then refutes this by noting that the attributes are described as eternal, and the defense merely redefines 'qadīm' to avoid the problem. The defense tries to distinguish between different meanings of 'qadīm', but the commentator insists that the objection remains because the state, like the attributes, is not eternal yet is still dependent on another. The commentator concludes by rejecting the defense as verbal wordplay, not conceptual. The passage also discusses the nature of causality: the cause of need for existents is temporal origination, not absolute need.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari defense, why do attributes not require a cause?
A) Because they are eternal and therefore uncaused
B) Because they are states (aḥwāl) and are not described as eternal
C) Because God creates them directly without a cause
D) Because they are identical to God's essence

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari defense hinges on the concept of 'state' (ḥāl) being non-eternal, thus no causal dependence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Ash'aris argue that God's attributes are not separate entities but states inhering in His essence. Do you often imagine God's attributes—like His mercy or His power—as distinct 'things'? How might that mental habit subtly undermine your tawḥīd? Commit today to consciously affirm that every attribute is nothing other than what He is.
?
The passage states that the cause of need is temporal origination (ḥudūth). Everything in your life—your health, your imān, your very breath—is temporally originated. In what specific area are you behaving as if something is self-sufficient, independent of God's constant causation? Name one thing you will acknowledge as contingent today.
?
If the attributes are 'states' that are not eternal, then God's mercy, for example, is not a timeless frozen quality but a dynamic relation to creation. Does your worship reflect that God's mercy is actively reaching you right now, or do you treat it as a distant fact? What would change if you truly believed His mercy is a present state directed at you this moment?

Refuting the Defense: Verbal Wordplay, Not Conceptual Solution
Refutation of the Ash'ari defense as mere verbal redefinition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari defense is rejected as mere verbal wordplay, by examining the refutation that redefining 'qadīm' does not solve the problem.

Core Idea
Redefining terms cannot hide the metaphysical problem.

The Ash'ari defense attempted to avoid the problem of causal dependence for eternal attributes by redefining 'qadīm' and invoking states. The commentator refutes this by showing that the state itself is neither eternal nor temporal, and that the defense is merely verbal manipulation. This lesson examines the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note that the refutation begins by dismissing any attempt to reinterpret the Ash'ari statements as concessions.
2
Trace the argument against redefinition
The refutation points out that the state is not described as temporal either, so how can it depend on another? The commentator also notes that changing the definition of 'qadīm' does not solve the issue because the discussion is about the eternal in the sense of what has no beginning of existence.
3
Understand the final dismissal
The commentator concludes that such apologies are 'verbal matters, not conceptual' (amūr lafẓiyya lā ma'nawiyya). Reflect on what this means for theological argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (قد يعتذر عن ذلك إلخ) يعني أنهم غير قائلين فيما ذكر من الأقوال باستناد القديم إلى العلة، لأن الحال لا يوصف بالقدم والصفات لاستنادها إلى ذاته تعالى وهي ليست مغايرة له لا استناد لها إلى علة لأن العلة يجب أن تكون مغايرة لمعلولها، فهذه الأقوال منهم لا تنافي ما يتصور منهم القول بأن القديم لا يستند إلى الموجب وأما أن هذه الأقوال منافية لما قالوا : من أن علة الحاجة هو الحدوث، فبحث آخر وجوابه : أن ذلك القول منهم إنما هو في الموجودات المغايرة لذاته تعالى . قلنا من أنه أي لاعلة حاجة له؛ لأن علة الحاجة عندهم هو الحدوث الزماني، إما مستقلاً أو على وجه الشطرية أو الشرطية . قوله : ( ولا مجال لتأويل التنزل فيها لأنها ثابتة منهم بلا تردد ولا ريب والتنزل أن يكون لو كان العلة هي الإمكان فرضاً وتسليماً لأمكن استناد القديم إلى العلة. قوله بأن القديم مالا أول لوجوده المتصف بالقدم والحدوث حقيقة هو الوجود، وأما الموجود فباعتباره، وقد يوصف به العدم ،فيقال للعدم الغير المسبوق بالوجود قديم، وللمسبوق حادث كذا في شرح المقاصد لكن المبحث هاهنا هو القديم بمعنى ما لا أول لوجوده، فلم يتجه الإشكال المذكور بقي فيه بحث وهو أن الحال كما لا يوصف بالقدم لا يوصف بالحدوث فكيف جوزوا استناده إلى الغير مع أنه لاعلة حاجة فيه، ويمكن أن يقال : علة احتياج الموجودات هي الحدوث لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً قوله : (إلا أن يغير تفسيره فحينئذ يوصف الحال بالعدم، لكن لا يرد الإشكال حينئذ أيضاً؛ لما أشرنا إليه الآن من أن الحدوث عندهم علة الاحتياج إلى المؤثر الموجد، لا علة الاحتياج مطلقاً .

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That redefining 'qadīm' or appealing to 'state' actually resolves the problem of eternal attributes depending on a cause.
Correction: The refutation shows that the state is neither eternal nor temporal, so the problem remains; the defense merely plays with words.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the defense as 'verbal, not conceptual'?
A) Because the defense contradicts scripture
B) Because the defense relies on redefining terms without solving the underlying problem
C) Because the Ash'aris never actually held that view
D) Because the defense proves the attributes are temporal

Key Takeaway
The refutation shows that redefining terms does not solve the core problem; the defense is dismissed as verbal wordplay.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological defense that sounds plausible, do you settle for verbal redefinitions rather than pressing deeper into the underlying reality? This lesson exposes the danger of being satisfied with words. Will you commit to examining arguments for conceptual substance, even when they come from respected authorities?
?
How often do you accept explanations that merely shift definitions without solving the core problem in your own understanding of Allah's attributes? Are you willing to endure the discomfort of unresolved questions rather than embracing verbal comfort?
?
The commentator dismisses the defense as 'verbal matters, not conceptual.' Is there an area in your faith where you rely on wordplay to avoid addressing a difficult truth? Will you set aside that crutch today and seek genuine understanding?
